<DDP_Bubble.node_security.nsjstatisticsdaily>

Command Type: This is the command type.

Num of Workflows: This is the total number of workflows.

Num of Success Workflows: This is the total number of successful workflows.

Num of Error Workflows: This is the total number of Error workflows.

Min Duration of Success Workflows: This is the minimum duration if all the workflows in (HH:MM:SS)

Max Duration of Success Workflows: This is the maximum duration of all the workflows in (HH:MM:SS)

Avg Duration of Success Workflows: This is the average duration of all the workflows in (HH:MM:SS)

This shows a count of jobs broken down by result and job type.

</DDP_Bubble.node_security.nsjstatisticsg> <DDP_Bubble.ops.ops_compsessions>


OPS Session is unique identity for any script execution. OPS session is completed when script execution is done for CLI and for GUI when it is closed. The table shows data for Successful and Failed CLI sessions along with GUI sessions closed during the day on each OPS VM.

  • Successful CLI Sessions: A CLI session is successful if it ends with normal program termination. The graph shows count of CLI sessions successfully executed without any error on each OPS VM.
  • Failed CLI Sessions: A CLI session is Failed if it does not end with normal program termination. It could be due to any error or exception found during script execution. The graph shows count of such failed CLI sessions on each OPS VM.

  • Non-parallel VM's like solr,openidm etc will display same JMX data for their offline and online links.DpmediationSasClientInstrumentationBeanenm_ebsl_inst_statsbslstreamGUI Sessions Completed: A GUI session is completed when it is closed. The graph shows count of GUI sessions closed on each OPS VM.

  • CLI Sessions Active:Count of CLI sessions running script towards Node on each VM.

  • GUI Sessions Active: Active GUI sessions shown currently opened GUI sessions on each VM.

</DDP_Bubble.ops.ops_compsessions> <DDP_Bubble.ops.winfiol_commands>

This graph shows the number of commands run on each cluster.

</DDP_Bubble.ops.winfiol_commands> <DDP_Bubble.ops.winfiol_sessions>

A WinFIOL session is responsible for connecting and sending/receiving data from a network element.

This data is to track number of ‘WinFIOL sessions’ OPS GUI spawns on each cluster per minute.

A session can have two different states:

  • Connected: The Session where able to connect toward a network element.
  • Failed: The connection toward a network element couldn’t be established.

Data is collected from Apache logs and is based on the breadcrumb in the GUI. If a user bookmarks a page or navigates to a page with right click actions etc. then we would not expect to see each stage of the breadcrumb e.g.  we may see the root breadcrumb once e.g. "Software and Hardware Manager" but it could also appear in other breadcrumbs e.g. for "Node Restart Job" if the "Node Restart Job" page was launched indirectly.

|Software and Hardware Manager |3|
|Software and Hardware Manager>Backup Administration>Create Backup Job |1|
|Software and Hardware Manager>Node Restart Job |8|

Data is collected from the following MBean: TBA.

  • Select Mediation Service:  Number of requests sent to the specific router policy.
  • Average Select Mediation Time: Average time it took the specific router policy to indicate which mediation service should process the MTR based on certain rules for stickiness, round robin etc. This does not involve the EJB call to the Policy Router.

</DDP_Bubble.mediationfwk.selectms> <DDP_Bubble.queue_topic_analysis.Maximum_delivery_attempts_exceeded_table>

This table shows the queus and topics where the maximum delivery attempts have been exceeded.

  • Total Count: This is the sum of all the times the message "maximum delivery attempts have been exceeded" was logged.
  • Max Count: This is the count of all the the message "maximum delivery attempts have been exceeded" was logged for the worst day.
  • Min Count: This is the count of all the the message "maximum delivery attempts have been exceeded" for the best day.

</DDP_Bubble.queue_topic_analysis.Maximum_delivery_attempts_exceeded_table> <DDP_Bubble.queue_topic_analysis.Queue_is_full_table>

  • Total Count: This is the sum of all the times the message "queue or topic is full" was logged.
  • Max Count: This is the count of all the the message "queue or topic is full" was logged for the worst day.
  • Min Count: This is the count of all the the message "queue or topic is full" for the best day.

</DDP_Bubble.mediationfwk.ClusteredEventBasedMediationClient> <DDP_Bubble.cm_domainproxy.sas>

Data is collected from the following MBean:

  • com.ericsson.oss.sas.common.metrics.domain-proxy-service:type=DomainProxyInstrumentation

Attributes:

  • De-registration Requests: Requests to de-register a CBSD from a SAS.
  • De-registration Responses: Responses from a SAS indicating a successful/unsuccessful CBSD de-registration.
  • Grant Requests: Requests of spectrum from a CBSD to a SAS.
  • Grant Responses: Responses from a SAS allocating spectrum to a CBSD.
  • Heartbeat Requests: Requests of access to allocated spectrum from a CBSD to a SAS.
  • Heartbeat Responses: Responses from a SAS suspending, terminating or granting access to allocated spectrum for a CBSD.
  • Spectrum Inquiry Requests: Requests of information on spectrum for a CBSD from a SAS.
  • Spectrum Inquiry Responses:  Responses of potential channel availability for a CBSD from a SAS.

  • Terminated Grants: Number of grants terminated by a SAS (response 500).
  • Relinquished Grants: Number of grants relinquished by Domain Proxy.
  • Revoked Grants: Number of grants revoked i.e. terminated (500), expired or auto de-registration from SAS (105).
  • Suspended Grants: Number of grants suspended by a SAS (response 501).
  • Failed Registrations: Number of failed CBSD registrations e.g. response 102 MISSING_PARAM.

All the DDC logs including the server, VCS, LITP, mcollective, Apache access & Elasticsearch logs are available on an NFS share. Click here for more information on how to access these logs (or) use the showmount command for the relevant server e.g. "showmount -e ddpi.athtem.eei.ericsson.se " from a linux shell e.g. from the MS and mount accordingly.

If the DDC log collection limits of 1 GB compressed (256MB for Vapps) have been exceeded the error "maxsize exceeded" will be seen in the table below. No further ElasticSearch collection will occur after the limit is reached but other instrumentation files will be collected.

If the DDC query to Elasticsearch times-out (default 300 seconds) the error "maxtime exceeded" will be seen.

Information about the files DDC collects is here.

Data  is collected from the Elasticsearch logs.

  • Job Type:  Use Case executed by operator.
  • Job Name: Main Job name provided by operator during Job creation
  • Number of networkElements: NetworkElement types which are part of current job
  • Start Time: Main job creation start time
  • End Time: Main job creation emd time
  • Total Time: Total duration of Main job completion
  • Progress Percentage:  The percentage of tasks that have been completed. Each backup consists of a numner of tasks so this is the number of tasks that bave been completed.
  • Status: Current state of Main Job
  • Result:   Result upon Current Main Job execution (Combination of all NE Jobs)


</DDP_Bubble.shmcoreserv_job_instrumentation.enm_shmcoreserv_details> <DDP_Bubble.shmcoreserv_job_instrumentation.enm_nhc_details>

Data  is collected from the Elasticsearch logs.

  • Job Type:  Use Case executed by operator.
  • Job Name: Main Job name provided by operator during Job creation
  • NeType: NetworkElement types which are part of current job
  • Number of networkElements: Number of NetworkElements that are part of main job
  • Start Time: Main job creation start time
  • End Time: Main job creation start time
  • Total Time: Total duration of Main job completion
  • Progress Percentage:  Aggregation of total nodes completion percentage
  • Category: Health Check Category on whicj job is executed
  • Nodes Health Status Count: Grouping of nodes based on the health status. Each node health status would be set upon Healthcheck execution
  • Status: Current state of Main Job
  • Result:   Result upon Current Main Job execution (Combination of all NE Jobs)

This data is taken from the Elasticsearch/Logstash log server where MO entry and exit points for 'Add-Node' use case are logged.

  • NE Time: The difference in milliseconds between NetworkElement MO entry and exit points.
  • CPP Time: The difference in milliseconds between CppConnectivityInformation MO entry and exit points.
  • Total Time: The sum of 'NE Time' and 'CPP Time' in milliseconds.

For more information click here.

</DDP_Bubble.asrl.Asrl_Instrumentation> <DDP_Bubble.EsxiStat.storageContentHelp>

CPU metrics data is fetched from "perfManager" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API and put in esxi_metrics.txt.

  • cpu.ready.summation(millisecond): Time that the virtual machine was ready.CPU ready time is dependent on the number of virtual machines on the host and their CPU loads.
  • cpu.costop.summation(millisecond): Amount of time a Symmetric Multi Processing(SMP) virtual machine was ready to run, but incurred delay due to co-vCPU scheduling contention.

</DDP_Bubble.EsxiStat.storageContentHelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.ServerHardware>

Server hardware information is retrieved from the output of the following commands.
prtdiag and prtconf

The configuration is only updated once per day. The following information is presented:

Server Type: this is retrieved from the System Configuration line of the prtdiag output
Memory: this is retrieved from the Memory Size line of the prtdiag output
CPU (Solaris)
CPUs are listed by prtdiag. The output of this command can be very different depending on the CPU archtecture, so there are a number of regular expressions used to parse several known CPU types. The heading Normalised CPU Performance is a metric used by the hardware dimensioning tool to provide a baseline CPU against which different CPU types can be compared. Unknown value in Normalised CPU Performance means it is not been defined in Hardware Dimensioning Tool
CPU (Linux)
CPUs are listed using the prtdiag command. In the case of a server type of Red Hat KVM, one CPU maps to a CPU as seen from the perspective of /proc/cpuinfo. In reality, one CPU in a VM maps to a core per thread on the bare metal server.
Storage: if there are storage arrays attached to the master server, and DDC has been able to retrieve information about them using the sccli command, then this information will be presented here.

Small ENM:

Server hardware information is retrieved from "host.Summary" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API

cENM:

</DDP_Bubble.server.ServerHardware> <DDP_Bubble.server.cpuHelp>

CPU usage information is retrieved from the server using the sar -A command. Data is only stored if there CPU activity.

Small ENM:

CPU metrics data is fetched from "perfManager" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API.

  • cpu.usage.average(%): Actively used CPU of the host, as a percentage of the total available CPU.

</DDP_Bubble.server.cpuHelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.dailyavghelp>

The table presents the daily average CPU usage, while the graph presents the CPU load across the day. The metrics presented are retrieved using the command sar -A.

The following metrics are presented:

  • Usr+Guest: the percentage of CPU time spent executing application code.
  • Sys: the percentage of CPU time spent executing system calls in the kernel.

  • IO Wait: purported to be the percentage of time spent waiting for IO. In reality this is a pretty useless metric as it is difficult for the kernel to calculate accurately, and since Solaris 10 this is always 0.

  • Steal: Percentage of time spent in involuntary wait by the virtual CPU or CPUs while the hypervisor was servicing another virtual processor.
  • Total: the total percentage of CPU time spent doing stuff - i.e. %Usr + %Guest + %Sys + %IO Wait + %Steal.

Small ENM:

  • Guest: Average CPU of the host from cpu.usage.average.

cENM:

This is taken from the node exporter via Prometheu and stored in a file e.g. remote_writer/dump.001.gz.

  • node_cpu_seconds_total: Each sample has a "mode" which determines whether is sys, user, iowait or steal.

</DDP_Bubble.server.dailyavghelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.prochelp>

Process count information is retrieved from the server using the command

sar -A

The data which this command outputs comes from the sa1 script running in the crontab of the sys
user account. see man sar and man sa1 for more details.

Note that, if you are monitoring a Linux server, the process count includes all threads running on
the system as well as their controlling processes.

Small ENM:

Currently we are not collecting process metrics for Small ENM

</DDP_Bubble.server.prochelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.procSechelp>

Processes per second is taken from sar output. The metric we graph depends on the server type.

Solaris

For Solaris systems we count the number of invocations of the fork system call, since this
directly correlates with the number of new process images created. Note that this means scripts which
replace their own image with a new binary by calling exec will be treated as a single process, since
the exec system call does not create a new process image.

Linux

On Linux systems, the sar command takes its metric from the /proc/stat file, namely the "processes" entry.
This value also includes the number of threads started as well as processes.
This is because on Linux a thread is closer to a full process in it's own right, with its own
process ID.

Small ENM:

Currently we are not collecting process metrics for Small ENM

</DDP_Bubble.server.procSechelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.MemoryHelp>

Memory information is retrieved using the "sar -A" command.

Solaris Notes:

The free ram graph on a Solaris system represents the amount of memory available to processes.

Linux Notes:

Free memory is memory not currently used by applications, in buffers or cached.

Used memory includes kernel memory which can sometimes incorporate large sections for inode_cache and dentry. These can be seen with  cat /proc/slabinfo and  cat /proc/meminfo.

Small ENM:

Memory metrics data is fetched from "perfManager" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API.

  • mem.usage.average(percent): Amount of used memory. Sum of the memory used by all powered on virtual machines and vCenter services on the host.

cENM:

This is taken from the node exporter via Prometheu and stored in a file e.g. remote_writer/dump.001.gz.

  • node_memory_MemFree_bytes: Each sample..
  • node_memory_Buffers_bytes: Each sample..
  • node_memory_Cached_bytes: Each sample..
  • node_memory_MemTotal_bytes: Each sample..

</DDP_Bubble.server.MemoryHelp> <DDP_Bubble.server.NetworkInterfaceHelp>

Soalris

Currently there are two different ways for us to collect network interface data from Solaris platforms. The original method is to collect the number of packets sent and received using the netstat -i command.

More recently - in the ERICddc product - we have been able to collect kernel statistics using the kstat interface, and can collect the bytes sent and received at a finer granularity. We specifically collect the kstats corresponding to:

nic-driver:nic-instance:nic-name:obytes64 nic-driver:nic-instance:nic-name:rbytes64

These values are converted into a rate by calculating the time delta and the bytes delta between two time periods and dividing the number of bytes by the number of seconds. This data is stored in the nic_stat table in the DDP database.

ENM

sar is used to collect network usage data.

ENM interface usage:

  • br0: Services
  • br1: Internal
  • br2: Storage
  • br3: JGroups

SMALL ENM:

Network metrics data is fetched from "perfManager" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API.

  • net.received.average(kiloBytesPerSecond): Average rate at which data was received during the collection interval. This represents the bandwidth of the network
  • net.transmitted.average(kiloBytesPerSecond): Average rate at which data was transmitted during the collection interval. This represents the bandwidth of the network
  • net.packetsRx.summation(number): Number of packets received during the collection interval
  • net.packetsTx.summation(number): Number of packets transmitted during the collection interval.

</DDP_Bubble.server.NetworkInterfaceHelp> <DDP_Bubble.storage.StorageContent>

Disk information is retrieved using 

sar -A

Small ENM:

Disk metrics data is fetched from "perfManager" object executed on ESXI host through Pyvmomi API.

  • disk.read.average(kiloBytesPerSecond): Rate at which data is read from each Logical Unit Number(LUN) on the host.
  • disk.write.average(kiloBytesPerSecond): Rate at which data is written to each Logical Unit Number(LUN) on the host.

</DDP_Bubble.enm_geo_kpi.GEO-RApplications> <DDP_Bubble.service.ddpServiceDataRentention>

These are the currently configured limits for DB and file retention.

DB means all the data in the SQL (live and replication) database.

Files means all the files that DDP stores after processing i.e. parsed logs, summarised logs and all other files collected by DDC that are available on the NFS mount or through the file search option in DDP.

In some cases they may be more data available than the supported limits if there is existing space available to temporarily support data retention for more time than the declared and formally supported limits.

Default DB retention is unlimited unless otherwise stated.

This data is taken from the EMC NAR files. The files are collected using the analyzer option of the naviseccli command.The files must be visible on SPA to be collected by DDC. The full output can be seen by searching for "nar" in the file search menu option.

There are a number of ways to find a volume UUID in openstack:

 1. In openstack use commands like "openstack volume list" and "openstack volume show <Volume UUID>"

 2. In the ENM CM "cat /etc/heat_user_data/cinder_bindings"

To find more about the volume from a storage viewpoint, search for the UUID found above, in the arrayconfig output. The arrayconfig output file can be got  by searching for "arrayconfig" using the file search menu option.

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PUSH") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 24 Hour ROPs 
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC.

Whethere a node is push or pull is determined by fileCollectionCategories.txt provided by PM.

</DDP_Bubble.pm_push_audit.1440MIN_PUSHflsROPHelp> <DDP_Bubble.pm_push_audit.15MIN_PUSHflsROPHelp>

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PUSH") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:00, hh:15, hh:30 or hh:45.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:00, hh:15, hh:30 or hh:45 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:30 and hh:45 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

Whethere a node is push or pull is determined by fileCollectionCategories.txt provided by PM.

</DDP_Bubble.pm_push_audit.15MIN_PUSHflsROPHelp> <DDP_Bubble.pm_med.15MIN_PULLflsROPHelp>

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:35 and hh:50 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

Whethere a node is push or pull is determined by fileCollectionCategories.txt provided by PM.

Data is collected from the  API for instrumentation to the source will be in eventdata.log.gz.n.

  • JOBID: Unique Identifier of the job

There are a number of ways to find a volume UUID in openstack:

  1.  In openstack use commands like "openstack volume list" and "openstack volume show <Volume UUID>"
  2.   In the ENM CM "cat /etc/heat_user_data/cinder_bindings"

To find more about the volume from a storage viewpoint, search for the UUID found above, in the arrayconfig output. The arrayconfig output file can be got  by searching for "arrayconfig" using the file search menu option.

  • MSSNMPCM Instance: The instance number of the MSSNMPCM cluster

  • Avg Duration: The average duration time [hh:mm:ss] of syncs on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals 
  • Avg MOs/Sec: The average number of Managed Objects per second synced on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals 
  • Max Duration: The maximium duration [hh:mm:ss] of a sync on the specified Instance or the maximum duration across all Instances where Instance equals Totals 
  • Total MOs Created/Updated: The total number of Managed Objects created/updated on the specified Instance or the total created/updated across all Instances where Instance equals Totals 
  • Total MOs Deleted: The total number of Managed Objects deleted on the specified Instance or the total deleted across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Total MOs Synced: The total number of Managed Objects synced on the specified Instance or the total synced across all Instances where Instance equals Totals 

  • Avg Data Retreival Time: The average time taken to retrive MIB data on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals. 

  • Avg Data Transformation Time: The average time taken to transform MIB data to U-NRM on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals .

  • Avg Data Writing Time: The average time taken for saving MIB data on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances into DPS where Instance equals Totals.

</DDP_Bubble.mssnmpcm.minilink_table> <DDP_Bubble.vnflaf_workflows.workflows>

</DDP_Bubble.mssnmpcm.Route_Instrumentation> <DDP_Bubble.postgres.enm_postgres_stats_db>

This data is taken from pg_stat_database view, that will contain one row for each database in the cluster, showing database-wide statistics.

  • Backends : The number of backend processes launched by server
  • Rows inserted : Number of rows inserted by queries in this database
  • Rows fetched : Number of rows fetched by queries in this database
  • Rows returned : Number of rows returned by queries in this database
  • Rows deleted : Number of rows deleted by queries in this database
  • Rows updated : Number of rows updated by queries in this database
  • Tx commited : Number of transactions in this database that have been committed
  • Tx rolled back : Number of transactions in this database that have been rolled back
  • Blocks Hit : Number of times disk blocks were found already in the buffer cache, so that a read was not necessary (this only includes hits in the PostgreSQL buffer cache, not the operating system's file system cache)
  • Blocks Read : Number of disk blocks read in this database
  • Queries Cancelled - Conflicts : Number of queries canceled due to conflicts with recovery in this database. (Conflicts occur only on standby servers; see pg_stat_database_conflicts for details.)
  • Deadlocks : Number of deadlocks detected in this database
  • Temp Bytes : Total amount of data written to temporary files by queries in this database. All temporary files are counted, regardless of why the temporary file was created, and regardless of the log_temp_files setting.
  • Temp Files : Number of temporary files created by queries in this database. All temporary files are counted, regardless of why the temporary file was created (e.g., sorting or hashing), and regardless of the log_temp_files setting.

</DDP_Bubble_19_Cmserv_Cli_Statistics_ScriptEngine_SessionFacade_Delegate> <DDP_Bubble_21_MessagesForHost>

LOG_LIMIT_EXCEEDED - DDP has the following two thresholds for processing logs:

  • Log count of 1,000,000 lines per server.
  • Log size of 1 GB per server.

If the logs of any given server crosses any of the two thresholds above DDP displays "LOG_LIMIT_EXCEEDED" as log message for all these post-threshold logs. It indicates that DDP has not processed those additional log lines for the relevant programs.

MAX_ROWS_EXCEEDED - DDP will limit the number of rows it displays in this table to 1,000 to prevent the browser crashing. If that limit is exceeded a row will be displayed showing the number of rows that are not displayed. The parsed log is available in a file called hosts.zip and it limited to 1,000 rows.

The below table can contain the following columns:

  • Program - The program or container which logged the message.
  • Severity - The severity of the logged message.
  • Count - The number of times this message occurred for this day.
  • First Time - The first time the message was seen this day.
  • Last Time -  The last time the message was seen this day.
  • Message - This is the generalized message with values such as ids and numbers extracted as [NUM]. To see the actual data the log file can be downloaded from the logs page.

If the thread name and logger are provided in the stack trace, they will also be shown at the top of the stack trace.

</DDP_Bubble_21_MessagesForHost> <DDP_Bubble_22_fmbnsi_Stats_E2E_Help>

 Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.nbi.fm.bnsi.utils.bnsi-server:type=TestInstrumentedBean


Attributes:

  • alarmsTranslated: The number of alarms translated by BNSI.
  • apsAlarmsTranslated: The number of spontaneous alarms translated by BNSI.
  • totalDelay: The total time that the asynchronous alarms used to rise from DB to ENM BNSI NBI.
  • totalDelayOnlyBnsi: The total time that the asynchronous alarms need to be managed by BNSI NBI (from the moment they enter the BNSI to the time they leave BNSI ).
  • counterOverTimeMax: The number of alarms exceeding the threshold of 5 sec within which each alarm is expected to be visible in NBI from the arrival in ENM.

</DDP_Bubble_24_Cmserv_Cli_Statistics_ScriptEngine_Scripting_Command_Resource_SessionFacade_Delegate> <DDP_Bubble.elasticsearch.enm_logs>

The table summarizes the analysis carried out on the elasticsearch logs of all the servers/pods.

  • Host: For each server/pod, clicking the link available against its hostname will present the generalized summary of elasticsearch messages logged by various programs on that particular server. 

In some cases the host can be see as "Unknown" and this can happen when messages are logged through rsyslogd before rsyslogd knows the hostname i.e, before host is present in ENM LITP model for physical deployments or known to Consul for vENM. (which can happen when VMs are initially created).

In cloud native systems pods are treated like servers and pod names are mapped to application names. The mapping to the actual pod name is shown when the log link is clicked.

When cloud native system are re-installed, logs from the pods  prior to the re-install will be still shown for this day. Consequently the same host type may appear twice - once for the previous instance of the pod and once for the current instance of the pod.

  • Log Entries: The total number of messages logged in the elasticsearch logs for the given server.
  • Log Size (KB): The total size (in KB) of messages logged in the elasticsearch logs for the given server.

Note #1:  DDC does not collect DEBUG level log entries so they will not be seen in any DDP analysis or be available in the "*.csv.gz" files.

To check pENM handler status e.g. for mscm: 

for ip in `awk '{print $2}' /etc/hosts | grep "mscm$" `;do echo "============ ${ip} ==========="; ssh -i /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@`echo $ip` '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging:read-children-resources\\(recursive=true,child-type=custom-handler\\)';done

To check pENM logger status e.g. for mscm:

for ip in `awk '{print $2}' /etc/hosts | grep "mscm$" `;do echo "============ ${ip} ==========="; ssh -i /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@`echo $ip` '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging:read-children-resources\\(recursive=true,child-type=logger\\)';done

To check pENM root logger status e.g. for mscm: 

 for ip in `awk '{print $2}' /etc/hosts | grep "mscm$" `;do echo "============ ${ip} ==========="; ssh -i /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@`echo $ip` '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging:read-children-resources\\(recursive=true,child-type=root-logger\\)';done

Note #2: To turn off all logging various options are available depending on the need e.g. for svc-1-impexpserv:

Stop pENM root logger logs going to ES:

ssh -i  /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@svc-1-impexpserv '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging/root-logger=ROOT:remove-handler\\(name="SYSLOG"\\)'

Stop pENM ITPF (recording API) error logs going to ES:

ssh -i  /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@svc-1-impexpserv '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging/logger=com.ericsson.oss.itpf.ERROR_LOGGER:remove-handler\\(name="SYSLOG_RECORDING"\\)'

Disable pENM handler for non ITPF (non recording API) logs so they will not go to ES:

ssh -i  /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@svc-1-impexpserv '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging/custom-handler=log4jappender:disable'

Stop pENM logging for a particular package e.g. for com.versant.odbms.XAResourceImpl:

ssh -i /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@svc-7-msapgfm '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging/logger=com.versant.odbms.XAResourceImpl:add'

ssh -i /root/.ssh/vm_private_key cloud-user@svc-7-msapgfm '/ericsson/3pp/jboss/bin/jboss-cli.sh -c --command=/subsystem=logging/logger=com.versant.odbms.XAResourceImpl:change-log-level\\(level=OFF\\)'

For more info on logging see the Application Logging Guidelines page.

</DDP_Bubble.elasticsearch.enm_logs> <DDP_Bubble.elasticsearch.ElasticSearch>

From the below table, the users can download the elasticsearch logs collected by DDC at regular intervals and then processed by DDP for enhanced readability of the logs.

  • Log File: Please 'Click' the link and 'Save' the file to your local system to download the given elasticsearch log file.

    A log file named "[0-9][0-9]_complete.csv.gz" (eg: 01_complete.csv.gz) will have the complete set of Elasticsearch logs collected by DDC for the given time interval. On the other hand, a log file named "[0-9][0-9]_partical.csv.gz" (eg: 01_partial.csv.gz) will have few logs missing for one or more servers (VMs or BMs) since the log counts of these servers for the given day have exceeded either one of the two log processing limits set for DDP (i.e., a log count of 1,000,000 lines per server [OR] a log size of 1 GB per server). A log file name such as "[0-9][0-9].csv.gz" (eg: 01.csv.gz) indicates that the "log completeness" check has not been performed for that file.

    Note 1: If even any single server (say "svc-1-ilogtoomuch") breaches the 1,000,000 log-count or 1 GB log-size in one of the very first log files (say "01_partial.csv.gz") itself then the rest of the log files for that day may also most likely get labelled as "[0-9][0-9]_partical.csv.gz" since they too will most likely have one or more log lines belonging to "svc-1-ilogtoomuch" server.

    Note 2: For any troubleshooting purposes the complete set of logs that are missing under "[0-9][0-9]_partical.csv.gz" files by looking into the raw DDC tar.gz files originally uploaded to DDP server from the given deployment.
  • Log File End Time: The time up to which the log data is available under the given elasticsearch log file. A value of 'NA' will be displayed under this field if DDP is unable to find the 'End Time' for this particular log file under database.
  • File Size (MB): The size of elasticsearch log file in Megabytes (MB). A value of '0' under this field doesn't necessary mean that the given log file is empty. The '0' values can appear due to limitations with bash arithmetic rounding for extremely small log files.

Note: The elasticsearch log files are available on the ENM system in the folder: /var/ericsson/ddc_data/<MS hostname>_TOR/<ddmmyy>/TOR/clustered_data/elasticsearch and in EIC are in the DDC pod in the folder /var/ericsson/ddc_data/ddcmaster/ddmmyy/elasticsearch/.

</DDP_Bubble.elasticsearch.ElasticSearch> <DDP_Bubble_25_Cmserv_Cli_Statistics_ScriptEngine_SCR_SFD>

This graph shows a breakdown of the time spent by the SCR and SFD components.

  • SFD Statistics: Sum of execution time of addCommand, getCommandStatus and getCommandResponse.
  • SCR - SFD Statistics:  Difference of Sum of execution time of submitCommand, getCommandStatus, getTerminalCommandOutput, getTerminalTextOutput and getObjectCommandOutput And Sum of execution time of addCommand, getCommandStatus and getCommandResponse.

</DDP_Bubble_25_Cmserv_Cli_Statistics_ScriptEngine_SCR_SFD> <DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.Successful_Amos_Commands>

This data is taken from the Elasticsearch/Logstash log server and is collected from the amos, scripting vms of the scripting nodes in general.

The table displays two columns namely Command and the Count.

  • Command: This attribute refers to name of the AMOS command executed successfully.
  • Count : Number of times the Specific command is executed successfully by any user.

Note: The command column sometimes displays the command value as a script when the actual amos command executed by any user contains atleast one special character like "/" ....

</DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.Successful_Amos_Commands> <DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.Amos_Users>

This data is taken from the Elasticsearch/Logstash log server and is collected from the amos, scripting vms of the scripting nodes in general. The actual usernames are not shown and they cannot be derived from the names shown. To find the actual usernames a seach in Elasticsearch is required.

The table displays two columns namely User and the Count.

  • User:  The hashed username of the user who executes the AMOS commands. The real username cannot be shown for privacy reasons. The hashed username can still show the same user activity over a period of time.
  • Count : Count refers to the number of the commands executed by the corresponding user.

</DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.Amos_Users> <DDP_Bubble.molist.MO_List_Table>

The MO (Managed Object), MO Count & Model Name are taken from the Versant object_count log file. The object_count log file gets populated by executing /opt/versant/bin/db2tty -D dps_integration.

The list displayed here is for only primary type MOs. Secondary object information is available from the raw DDP files.

Note: If the "MO Count" column is displayed, then it includes all MOs from both the "live" and "non-live" buckets. This can be seen with earlier DDC versions when the MO info per config was not collected.

</DDP_Bubble.molist.MO_List_Table> <DDP_Bubble_10_ENM_Health_Status_Versant>

For each Versant health-check one or more rows will appear in this table. DDP checks for the following health-checks:

  • Consistency Check : If no consistency check (CC) has been run for the given day then a single row will appear under the table with the status as  'Not Executed' . If CC has been run then multiple rows will appear under the table where each row presents the status of one of its milestones namely 'DB Backup', 'Versant CC', 'DPS CC' & 'Overall Status'. Please find below the different possible statuses for these milestones:
    1. CC Milestone 1: DB Backup
      1. 'Successful' : This status indicates that the latest database backup on the given day has been successful.
      2. 'Executed but Timed Out' : This status indicates that the latest database backup executed on the given day got timed out due to some reason.
      3. 'Executed but Failed/Terminated' : This status indicates that the latest database backup executed on the given day either got failed with some error or got terminated/killed by the user.
    2. CC Milestone 2: Versant CC
      1. 'Not Consistent' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC on the given day detected an inconsistency.
      2. 'Executed but Timed out' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC executed on the given day got timed out due to some reason.
      3. 'Executed but Failed/Terminated' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC executed on the given day either got failed with some error or got terminated/killed by the user.
      4. 'Not executed' : This status indicates that the Versant CC did not get executed in the latest CC run on the given day, most likely, due to failure or timeout of the upstream milestone (i.e., 'DB Backup').
    3. CC Milestone 3: DPS CC
      1. 'Not Consistent' : This status indicates that the latest DPS CC on the given day detected an inconsistency.
      2. 'Executed but Timed out' : This status indicates that the latest DPS CC executed on the given day got timed out due to some reason.
      3. 'Executed but Failed/Terminated' : This status indicates that the latest DPS CC executed on the given day either got failed with some error or got terminated/killed by the user.
      4. 'Not executed' : This status indicates that the DPS CC did not get executed in the latest CC run on the given day, most likely, due to failure or timeout of one of the upstream milestones (i.e., 'DB Backup' or 'Versant CC').
    4. CC Milestone 4: Overall Status
      This represents the overall status of the aforementioned CC milestones with the below possible statuses:
      1. 'Not Consistent' : This status indicates that the latest CC run on the given day has detected inconsistencies.
      2. 'Executed but Timed Out' : This status indicates that the latest CC executed on the given day has timed out at one of its aforementioned milestones.
      3. 'Executed but Failed/Terminated' : This status indicates that the latest CC executed on the given day either got failed with some error or got terminated/killed by the user at one of its aforementioned milestones.
        Note: A value of 'NA' in the table corresponds to 'Not Applicable'. The time of 'Overall Status' will be mostly displayed as 'NA' as it just presents the consolidated status of 'DB Backup', 'Versant CC' & 'DPS CC' milestones. An exception to this is the  'Not Consistent'  overall status whose time will correspond to the log lines reporting inconsistencies.
    Consistency Check (Older version): The older version of DDP's CC health-check used to represent the status of only 'Versant CC' milestone and didn't include the statuses of 'DB Backup' & 'DPS CC' milestones. So for all these older dates, a single row with the below statuses will still represent the CC.
      • 'Not Consistent' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC on the given day detected an inconsistency.
      • 'Executed but Timed out' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC executed on the given day got timed out due to some reason.
      • 'Executed but Failed/Terminated' : This status indicates that the latest Versant CC executed on the given day either got failed with some error or got terminated/killed by the user.
      • 'Not executed' : This status indicates the Versant CC did not get executed on the given day. Please note that the cases, where 'backup_and_consistency_check_database.sh' script got timed-out/failed/terminated at database backup stage itself and no 'consistency_check_database.sh' script has been run, will also get reported as 'Not executed' .

When a Versant DB has crashed, a row will be appeared in this table which contains the below attributes.

  • DB Crashed : This status indicates that the db has crashed on the given day.
  • Dead Transactions : This status indicates that the dead transactions are logged in elasticsearch. This will display the number of times it occurred.
  • Roll Back Transactions : This status indicates that the roll back transactions are logged in elasticsearch. This will display the number of times it occurred.

</DDP_Bubble_10_ENM_Health_Status_Versant> <DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Node_Stats>

</DDP_Bubble_34_ENM_LCM_Sentinel> <DDP_Bubble_35_ENM_FM_Alarm_Event_Stats>

DDP is getting the data from all.events file as per the severity of alarms as below.

NEW = x1
CHANGED = x2
ACK STATE CHANGED = x3
CLEARED = x4

An alarm event corresponds to one notification send by FM/FMS on the OSS. For a single alarm you will have two or more events (1 new alarm event, 1 cleared alarm event and maybe an ack state change event)
Note: An active node is defined as a node that sent one or more alarm events

Note: Total nodes per type is taken from the ONRM CS. Where node type is listed as "UNKNOWN_NODE_TYPE", this generally indicates a problem retrieving ONRM data from the CS and will result in the "Total Nodes" column being empty.;


All the alarms which are present in FMA_alarm_log will be not be present in all.events as:

1.When an alarm came to OSS with same alarm number which is already existing at OSS side(active) then the alarm will be dropped at kernel level and kept in FMA_alarm_log but
will not be forwarded to ALV or NMS i.e all.events.

2.If display status of alarm is 0 then also it will present in Database but not present in ALV and ddp and all.events.

3.Depending on stateAction attribute of Alarm also FM will not forward alarm to north bound.

Hence FM alarms count will differ from fma_alarm_log.

</DDP_Bubble_35_ENM_FM_Alarm_Event_Stats> <DDP_Bubble.ebsm_statistics.Nodes_Totals>

</DDP_Bubble.ebsm_statistics.Nodes_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_38_JMS_Active_Queue>

This data is retrieved from 'list-all-consumers-as-json'  file. 

An active queue/topic is one where there has been a non-zero value for messagesAdded or messageCount during the current day.

A JMS Queue implements load balancer semantics. A single message will be received by exactly one consumer. If there are no consumers available at the time the message is sent it will be kept until a consumer is available that can process the message.

If a consumer receives a message and does not acknowledge it before closing then the message will be redelivered to another consumer. A queue can have many consumers with messages load balanced across the available consumers.

For more information on the 3PP see the HornetQ docs here and for troubleshooting with DDP see here.

Information about each queue and topic is here.

</DDP_Bubble_38_JMS_Active_Queue> <DDP_Bubble_39_JMS_Active_Topic>

This data is retrieved from 'list-all-consumers-as-json'  file. 

An active queue/topic is one where there has been a non-zero value for messagesAdded or messageCount during the current day.

In JMS a Topic implements publish and subscribe semantics. When you publish a message it goes to all the subscribers who are interested - so zero to many subscribers will receive a copy of the message.

Only subscribers who had an active subscription at the time the broker receives the message will get a copy of the message. If no consumers exist when a message is sent – the message will be dropped.

For more information on the 3PP see the HornetQ docs here and for troubleshooting with DDP see here

</DDP_Bubble_39_JMS_Active_Topic> <DDP_Bubble_40_JMS_Plot_Queue>

This data is retrieved from 'list-all-consumers-as-json'  file. 

Instrumentation graphs are generated from JMX data collected from the JMS service:

  • Messages Added: Number of messages added to this queue.
  • Message Count: Number of messages currently held in this queue awaiting delivery.
  • Consumer Count: Number of consumers currently consuming messages from this queue.
  • Delivering Count: Number of messages that this queue is currently delivering to its consumers that have not been acknowledged.
  • Scheduled Count: Number of scheduled messages in this queue awaiting scheduled delivery.

Note: Information about each queue and topic is here.

</DDP_Bubble_40_JMS_Plot_Queue> <DDP_Bubble_41_JMS_Plot_Topic>

  • Message Count: Number of messages awaiting delivery for all subscribers for this topic.
  • Subscription count: Number of (durable and non-durable) subscribers for this topic.
  • Delivering Count: Number of messages that this topic is currently delivering to its consumers that have not been acknowledged.

</DDP_Bubble_43_Common_Topn_Plot_All_Graph_Guide> <DDP_Bubble_44_Common_Topn_Processes_List>

Metrics are taken from the file jps.log.

  • CPU: CPU is the total CPU time in minutes for the day.
  • Avg. CPU/Sec: Average CPU per Second is the time that CPU is used during a sample time period, which is then divided by this sample time period (in seconds). This then gives a percentage value if multiplied by 100.
  • Memory: Memory (RSS), Threads and File Descriptors are the peak values for the day.
  • [AGGREGATED]: Processes which use less than 50 mins CPU for the day or use less than 150MB max memory or have less that 100 max file descriptors or have less than 50 max threads are not listed separately. Instead they are "aggregated" into a single entry. To see the actual processes used to make this table search for jps.log in the file search which will show all the process at that snapshot in time.
  • [HOME_SCRIPT]: These are all processes that begin with /home or /$HOME or /export/home
  • [DOT_SCRIPT]: These are all processes that begin with ./
  • [TMP_SCRIPT]: These are all processes that begin with /tmp or /var/tmp
  • [ROOT_SCRIPT]:These are all processes that begin with /root
  • [SHELL_CMD]:These are all processes that have a shell in the command line i.e. (sh, csh, ksh, bash, tcsh, pfsh)

Note: As part of TORF-101684, "Memory" column is removed from DDP UI for ENM deployments only. This column would be still available in the excel downloads.

This is a list of all previously created queries. You can select an option, which will run the selected query.

</DDP_Bubble_68_ENM_Health_Status_Saved_Query_Presets> <DDP_Bubble_67_ENM_Network_Elements_Summary>

This table provides the information on Node Types present.

Currently NE Release, Functional MIM Name, and Functional MIM Version are only collected for ERBS nodes. This information is obtained from the database clusters and written to a file called neTypeInfo.txt 

Mim name and Mim version will be displayed only for CPP Nodes which does not have fragments.For Non CPP Nodes , A link has been provided in Model ID to see Mim name And Mim Version. 

Note: It is possible for a the Model ID to be blank as it may not be set in the source data. In the case of ERBS  nodes if the Model ID is blank then the NE Release, Functional MIM Name, and Functional MIM Version will be blank for those nodes as the Model ID is required to get that information.

</DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Mib_Upgrade> <DDP_Bubble_70_ENM_Overall_Summary>

An overall summary of time taken to perform the upgrade.

All the data except for "ENM From Version" are retrieved from the mentioned enminst.log file.

NOTE: Below enminst.log contains the upgrade details of today's data (When upgrade happens for 1 day)

In case of "Upgrade spanning for two days", then next day's log is to be downloaded from "Filesearch" option of next day's main page

Attributes:

  • ENM ISO: The ENM ISO which was installed.
    • Retrieved from the line where the command "- upgrade_enm.sh" is logged.
  • ENM From Version: The previous version of ENM prior to the upgrade.
    • This is retrieved from the file TOR/sw_inventory/enm-history based on the ISO version retrieved in the previous step.
  • LITP ISO: The ISO used to perform the upgrade.
    • Retrieved from the line where the command "- upgrade_enm.sh" is logged.
  • Upgrade Status: States whether an upgrade succeeded or failed.
    • Retrieved form the line where either "System upgrade failed" or "System successfully upgraded" is logged after plan execution.
  • Duration: The total amount of time taken to perform the upgrade based on the difference between the start and end time.
    • The Start time is based on when the command "- upgrade_enm.sh" is logged. 
    • The end time is based on when either "System upgrade failed" or "System successfully upgraded" is logged after plan execution.
  • <Cluster Type>_cluster: This repeats showing the name of each cluster and the total time spent being upgraded, based on the difference between the cluster start and end time.
    • The cluster start time is determined as the time of the first task performed on the cluster.
    • The end time is determined from either the start of a task on a different cluster or the end of the plan execution.
  • Other Time: The amount of time taken to perform the upgrade not related to the listed clusters.
    • This is the overall duration minus the total duration of cluster upgrades.

</DDP_Bubble_70_ENM_Overall_Summary> <DDP_Bubble_71_ENM_enm_upgrade_cluster_level_summary>

A summary of the time taken to upgrade each cluster. The times are taken from the enminst log file. The values in this table are retrieved from the tasks listed in the log file.

The task times are based on the difference between when tasks as logged with a state of "Initial>Running" and when they are logged with a state of "Running>Success".

The Lock, Upgrade, and Unlock values are totals of the time taken to perform those actions for each Node on the clusters.

Attributes:

  • Cluster: The cluster which was upgraded.
  • Total: This is the total time spent upgrading the cluster based on the difference between the cluster start and end time.
    • The cluster start time is determined as the time of the first task performed on the cluster.
    • The end time is determined from either the start of a task on a different cluster or the end of the plan execution.
  • Lock: The total time taken to lock the cluster.
  • Upgrade: The total time taken to upgrade the cluster.
  • Unlock: The total time taken to unlock the cluster.
  • Other: Other time taken to perform the upgrade.
    • Calculated by subtracting the lock, upgrade, and unlock times from the total.

</DDP_Bubble_71_ENM_enm_upgrade_cluster_level_summary> <DDP_Bubble_72_ENM_enm_upgrade_node_level_summary>

A summary of the time taken to upgrade each Node. The times are taken from the metrics.log file. The values in this table are retrieved from the tasks listed in the enminst.log file.

The task times are based on the difference between when tasks as logged with a state of "Initial>Running" and when they are logged with a state of "Running>Success".

Attributes:

  • Node: The node which was upgraded.
  • Start: The time at which the upgrade began.
  • Total: The total time taken to upgrade the node.
  • Lock: The time taken to lock the node.
  • Upgrade: The time taken to upgrade the node.
  • Unlock: The  time taken to unlock the node.

</DDP_Bubble_72_ENM_enm_upgrade_node_level_summary> <DDP_Bubble_73_ENM_WpServ_Node_Totals>

</DDP_Bubble_81_ENM_FmFmxServ_Node_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_82_ENM_FmFmx_Stats>

These instrumentation attributes are mainly for the alarms flowing between FM (fm-fmx-adaptor in fmalarmprocessing VM) and FMX. The alarm flow between FM & FMX is always subjected to the following:

  • FMX rules activated
  • Type of active rules
  • Triggers in each of the rule at FMX and
  • Alarms matched with the active rules at any point of time.

Out of all the instrumented attributes in fm-fmx-adaptor, not every alarm goes to AlarmProcessor. Only FMX Show/Hide, FMX Create and FMX Update are sent to APS and instrumented in the APS Received and APS Processed.

Other instrumented attributes in the fm-fmx-adaptor are not sent to APS. They are the alarm action updates (ACK, UNACK and CLEAR) sent to FMX from fm-fmx-adaptor based on the rule.

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBeans:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.fm.fmxadaptor.instrumentation.fm-fmx-adaptor:type=FmxadaptorInstrumentation

Total UnAcknowledgementsSent to FMX : UnAcknowledged Alarms forwarded to FMX after matching with the active FMX subscriptions.

Total Clears Sent to FMX : Clear Alarms forwarded to FMX after matching with the active FMX subscriptions.

Total Active FMX Subscriptions : Active FMX subscriptions exist in FM.

Total New Alarms Received From FMX : New alarms received from FMX.

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.fm.fmxadaptor.instrumentation.fm-fmx-adaptor:type=FmxadaptorRequestsInstrumentation

 Attributes:

Total Show Alarm Requests Received : Show alarm requests came from FMX.

Total Hide Alarm Requests Received : Hide alarm requests came from FMX.

Total Sync Requests Received From FMX : Sync alarms requests came from FMX.

Total Update Alarm Requests Received : Update alarm requests came from FMX.

Total Number of Alarms Sent to FMX : Total number of matched alarms being forwarded to FMX with the active subscriptions.

</DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.YANG_CRUD_Instrumentation> <DDP_Bubble_90_ENM_cmserv_Activation_History_Writer>

The CM Activation and History information  is retrieved from the ElasticSearch logs

Activation : This section holds details of the MOs activated as part of an activation job

  • Job Id : This is the unique job ID for the activation Job
  • Activation Start Time :  This is the time the activation job was started
  • Activation End Time : This is the time the activation job was finished, including the time to write history data.
  • Activation Duration :  Time in ms for the activation job to run.
  • Activation successfulChanges :  The number of MOs successfully activated
  • Activation failedChange :  The number of MOs which failed to activate
  • Activation Result :  SUCCESS - if all MOs were successfully activated, PARTIAL - if some MOs were not activated, FAILED - if none of the MOs were activated
  • Activation processedChangessPerSec :  This is the rate in MOs/second for all MOs (succcessfulChanges and failedChange)
  • Activation configName :  The name of the non live configuration which was activated.
  • Status Detail : This statement  shows activation status. For  "Status Detail" column we have used the below abbreviations.
    COMPLETED : COMPLETED
    COMPLETED_C_FAIL : COMPLETED Some applied change has failed
    COMPLETED_H_FAIL : COMPLETED Warning: History data not successfully stored. Please see online help.
    COMPLETED_CH_FAIL : COMPLETED Some applied change has failed. Warning: History data not successfully stored. Please see online help.
    NA / NULL : If the elasticsearch log do not have Status Detail attribute.

Historical Writer :  This section holds details of MOs to be written to the CM History. Only successfully activated MOs are stored here, so if no MOs were successfully activated ( i.e. successfulChanges in the Activation section is 0, these fields will be empty .)

  • Historical Start Time:  The time that writing to the CM history store has started
  • Historical End Time: The time that writing to the CM history store has finished 
  • Historical Duration: The time in ms for writing to the CM history store
  • History Percentage - Time to write the history data for a job as a percentage of the overall job time
  • Historical Total Mo To Write :  The number of MOs to write to CM history store. This will never be less than sucessfulChanges, but may be higher, since some activated MOs may result in other automatic changes, e.g. automatic deletion of child MOs)
  • Historical mib_root_created :  The number of MIB Root MOs created
  • Historical mo_created :  The number of non-MIB Root MOs created
  • Historical attribute_modification :   Then umber of MOs where attributes were modified
  • Historical mo_deleted :  The number of MOs deleted, note this will include MOs automatically deleted if a parent MO is deleted.
  • Historical action_performed :  The number of MOs where an MO action is called.
  • Historical size :   The total size in bytes written to the CM History store.
  • Historical Total Written :   The total number of MOS written to the CM History store. This will equal totalMoToWrite if the storage has been completely successful, or less, if there has been some failure.
  • Historical Average size :  The average size (in bytes) of the MOs to be written to the CM history store.
  • Max MO Per Write - Indicates the maximum number of MOs written to SOLR in one write operation for the job
  • Min MO Per Write - Indicates the minimum number of MOs written to SOLR in one write operation for the job
  • Avg MO Per Write - Indicates the average number of MOs written to SOLR in all write operations for the job

NOTE : Activation Result : This field will be blank , if the "result" field is not available in the cmserv log files.

             Historical Average size :   This field will be blank , if " Historical Total Written"   is zero

This table include a summary of all the history data written for a given activation job ID, which aggregates the data for each of the individual DB writes.

To see the details of each individual history write operation, select the link in the job ID for the activation job. This will open a new page with detailed information for all write operations for the selected job.

</DDP_Bubble_90_ENM_cmserv_Activation_History_Writer> <DDP_Bubble.shmcoreserv_job_instrumentation.mainJobs>

</DDP_Bubble_96_OSS_NMA_Daily_Statistics> <DDP_Bubble_97_OSS_NMA_Connection_Status_Events>

A connectionStatus event occurs when NMA connects or disconnects from a Node, for example when the node restarts.

This is a plot of the connectionStatus Events. Each position on the vertical axis represents a unqiue node.

Each point represents a time when NMA connected or disconnected from a node.

If the graph shows a vertical line of points, this represents when a batch of nodes all connect/disconnect at the same time.

If the graph shows a horizontal line of points, this represents a single node that NMA is repeatedly loosing/regaining connection with.

</DDP_Bubble_97_OSS_NMA_Connection_Status_Events> <DDP_Bubble_98_OSS_NMA_Instrumentation_Graphs>

</DDP_Bubble_99_OSS_NMA_Notifications_Received> <DDP_Bubble_100_Bulk_CM_Import>

The Bulk CM Import data is retrieved from the Elasticsearch logs. These Bulk CM Import values display the following information (A value of 'NA' under any given column of this table stands for "Not Available"):

  • Job Id: The Id of the import job.
  • Status: The status of the import job.
  • Copy Start: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the copy operation started for the import job.
  • Copy End: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the copy operation ended for the import job.
  • Copy Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the copy operation.
  • Import Start: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the import operation started for the import job.
  • Import End: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the import operation ended for the import job.
  • Import Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import operation.
  • Total Elapsed Time: The total time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import job (i.e., the time elapsed between 'Copy Start' and 'Import End').
  • Nodes Copied: The total number of nodes copied as part of the import job.
  • Nodes Not Copied: The total number of nodes not copied as part of the import job.
  • MOs Created: The total number of Managed Objects created.
  • MOs Updated: The total number of Managed Objects updated.
  • MOs Deleted: The total number of Managed Objects deleted.
  • File Format: The format of the file used for the import job.
  • Configuration: The name of the configuration used for the import job.
  • Import File: The name of the import file used for the import job.

Data is encapsulated in network packets, which provide the load in the network.

</DDP_Bubble_105_NIC_Traffic_Summary_LVSRouters> <DDP_Bubble_106_LVS_Traffic_Summary_LVSRouters>

This table shows the breakdown of network traffic on a particular VIP.

It shows the traffic received by a specific VIP and the destinations to which the traffic is then distributed.

For Physical Deployments:

Data comes from ipvsadm.log, ipvsadm_stats.log, nf_conntrack and ip_addr.log.

For cENM Deployments:

Data is collected from Prometheus app eric_l4_external_address.

Attributes:

  • Instance: The name of the ingress-l4 instance
  • External Address: The VIP name
  • External Port: The VIP port
  • Pod ID: The backend pod Name
  • Pod Port: The backend pod port
  • Protocol: The transport protocol used
  • Connections: The number of connections between the External Address/port and the backend pod port
  • Packets Received: The number of packets coming from the External Address/port to the backend pod port
  • Packets Sent: The number of outgoing packets from the backend pod port
  • Bytes Received: The number of bytes coming from the External Address/port to the backend pod port
  • Bytes Sent: The number of outgoing bytes from the backend pod port

Number of AC’s: Total number of Attachment Circuits included in the connectivity (across all the Network Elements)

Total Number of MO’s affected: Total number of Managed Objects created (deployed) or deleted (undeployed) or modified during the specified operation on a connectivity. Total includes MO's from all NE's and all AC's in a connectivity

</DDP_Bubble.ap_daily_metrics.deleteProjDaily> <DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Daily_Totals>

This information is generated from data collected from elasticsearch logs.

This Daily Total values display the following information:

  • MSCM Instance: The instance number of the MSCM cluster
  • Avg Duration: The average duration time [hh:mm:ss] of syncs on the specified MSCM Instance or the average across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

  • Avg MOs/Sec: The average number of Managed Objects per second synced on the specified MSCM Instance or the average across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

  • Max Duration: The maximum duration [hh:mm:ss] of a sync on the specified MSCM Instance or the maximum duration across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

  • Total MOs Created: The Total number of Managed Objects created on the specified MSCM Instance or the total created across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

  • Total MOs Deleted: The Total number of Managed Objects deleted on the specified MSCM Instance or the total deleted across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

  • Total MOs Synced: The Total number of Managed Objects synced on the specified MSCM Instance or the total across all MSCM Instances where MSCM Instance equals Totals

</DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Daily_Totals> <DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Sync_Success>

This data is taken from the Elasticsearch logs here each stage of a successfull sync is logged.

  • Duration: Duration of sync in milliseconds from when the sync was initiated in the flow
  • MOs: Total MOs synced
  • Attributes: Total attributes synced
  • MO/sec: Rate of MOs synced per second: (Total MOs synced)/(Total duration for sync)
  • Adjusted MO/sec: Rate of MOs synced per second using DPS time only: (Total MOs synced)/(DPS topology duration + DPS attribute duration). The goal of this derived metric is to remove the network/node f rom the sync performance metric as much as possible so as to better gauge of internal sync performance
  • NE Tolology: Time taken for the network element (NE) topology handler to get the topology from the NE
  • DPS Topology: Time taken for DPS topology handler to write the topology to the database. This includes the addition and deletion of MOs on the database to reflect the NE topology
  • NE Attribute: Time taken for the NE attribute handler to get the attributes from the NE
  • DPS Attribute: Time taken for DPS attribute handler to write the attributes to the database

For DELTA Syncs, some of the columns have different meanings:

  • NE Tolology: Time taken for the network element info handler to get info from the NE
  • NE Attribute: Time taken to read the changes from the NE
  • DPS Topology: Time taken to merge the changes
  • DPS Attribute: Time taken to write the changes to DPS
  • MOs Created: MOs created or updated
  • MOs Deleted: MOs deleted

</DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Sync_Success> <DDP_Bubble_123_ENM_Health_Status_CPP_Full_Hourly_Syncs>

A status of ' Amber ' will be seen if >1% of nodes were "Full" synced during any hour.

A status of ' Red ' will be seen if >2% of nodes were "Full" synced during any hour.

</DDP_Bubble_123_ENM_Health_Status_CPP_Full_Hourly_Syncs> <DDP_Bubble_124_OSS_PMS_File_Transfer_Statistics_per_ROP>

The following graphs are derived from data collected from /var/opt/ericsson/nms_umts_pms_seg/data/ftpDataOutput.txt


MB data collected - This shows the amount of data collected per ROP interval.

Number Files collected - This shows the amount of files collected per ROP interval.

ROP Duration- This shows how long it took for ROP to collect the files per ROP interval.

  • Duration is the difference between the time of the first and last collected file during that interval. 

Files Collection Distribution- This shows the amount of files collected per ROP interval.

  • The bars are stacked by smaller periods of time within that ROP interval. This breaks the interval down into 5 smaller periods.

Files Collected outside ROP - This shows the number of files collected outside the ROP interval.

</DDP_Bubble_124_OSS_PMS_File_Transfer_Statistics_per_ROP> <DDP_Bubble_125_OSS_PMS_Connection_Stats>

Data for the Connection statistics is collected from the nodeFtpdata logs in /var/opt/ericsson/ftpm/data/

These are stored in the ftpm directory in ddp.

</DDP_Bubble_125_OSS_PMS_Connection_Stats> <DDP_Bubble_126_OSS_PMS_File_Transfer_Statistics_per_Node_Type>

File transfer stats per node are parsed from file transfer data collected by PMS.
This data is collected from
/var/opt/ericsson/nms_umts_pms_seg/data/ftpDataOutput.txt

Node Type - This is derived from nodeFDN the ftpDataOutput file.

  • The node type is derived from the second 'SubNetwork' entry by mapping it to network element data stored in DDP.

File Type - This is derived from scannerType in the ftpDataOutput file.

  • A scanner type of 1 or 2 maps to the file type 'STATS'.
  • A scanner type of 3 maps to the file type 'CTR'.
  • A scanner type of 4 maps to the file type 'UETR'.
  • A scanner type of 5 maps to the file type 'GPEH'.
  • A scanner type of 6 maps to the file type 'CELLTRACE'.
  • A scanner type of 7 maps to the file type 'UETRACE'.

Period - This is the duration of the ROP Period. It is derived from filePriority in the ftpDataOutput file.

  • A priority of 0 is 15 every minutes.
  • A priority of 1 is 1 every minutes.
  • A priority of 5 is every 5 minutes.
  • A priority of 60 is every 60 minutes.

Num Files - Derived from the number of entries parsed in ftpDataOutput which matched the expected output.

Total (Mb) - The sum of (('bytestransferred' / 1024) + 0.5)

Average Throughput (B/s) - Calculated by getting the average of ((('bytesTransferred' * 1000) / 'duration') + 0.5).

Min. Throughput (B/S) - Calculated by getting the minimum of ((('bytesTransferred' * 1000) / 'duration') + 0.5).

</DDP_Bubble_126_OSS_PMS_File_Transfer_Statistics_per_Node_Type> <DDP_Bubble_127_OSS_PMS_Stats_Collection_Success_by_Node_Type>

Node Type - This is derived from nodeFDN in the ftpDataOutput file.

  • The node type is derived from the second "SubNetwork" by mapping it to network element data stored in DDP.

ROP Period - This is the duration of the ROP Period. It is derived from the priority in ftpDataOutput.

  • A priority of 0 is 15 every minutes.
  • A priority of 1 is 1 every minutes.
  • A priority of 5 is every 5 minutes.
  • A priority of 60 is every 60 minutes.

Available - Derived by checking the number of entries parsed in ftpDataOutput which matched the expected output while also compensating for missing files.

Not Collected - This is calculated by subtracting the number collected by the number available.

Success Ratio % - This is calculated with (100 * ('Available' - 'Not Collected') ) / 'Available'

</DDP_Bubble_127_OSS_PMS_Stats_Collection_Success_by_Node_Type> <DDP_Bubble_128_ENM_Apache_Totals>

  • Deletes are detected when an ATTRIBUTE_VALUE_CHANGE event contains a lastModification attribute with an Operator/X2/ANR deletion value

</DDP_Bubble_139_OSS_SON_qOffset_CIO_Changes> <DDP_Bubble.cm_imports.Bulk_CM_Import_old>

The Bulk CM Import data is retrieved from the Elasticsearch logs. These Bulk CM Import values display the following information (A value of 'NA' under any given column of this table stands for "Not Available"):

  • Job Id: The Id of the import job.
  • Status: The status of the import job.
  • Job Start: The start time [hh:mm:ss] of the import job.
  • Job End: The end time [hh:mm:ss] of the import job.
  • Copy Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the copy operation.
  • Parsing Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the parsing operation.
  • Import Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import operation.
  • Total Elapsed Time: The total time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import job (i.e., the time elapsed between 'Copy Start' and 'Import End').
  • Nodes Copied: The total number of nodes copied as part of the import job.
  • Nodes Not Copied: The total number of nodes not copied as part of the import job.
  • MOs Created: The total number of Managed Objects created.
  • MOs Updated: The total number of Managed Objects updated.
  • MOs Deleted: The total number of Managed Objects deleted.
  • MOs Processed/sec.execution phase: The total number of Managed Objects processed (i.e., MOs Created + MOs Updated + MOs Deleted) per second (of the import time).
  • File Format: The format of the file used for the import job.
  • Configuration: The name of the configuration used for the import job.
  • Import File: The name of the import file used for the import job.

Shows the Sync KPI Performance for the specified time period. Enter the below inputs and click 'update' to see the data in the table.

  • 'From': The start time of the time period for which Sync KPI Performance needs to be shown.
  • 'To': The end time of the time period for which Sync KPI Performance needs to be shown.
  • 'Network Element': This is an optional parameter that takes a network element name (FDN) as input. If network element name has been provided then Sync KPI Performance for that particular network element will be shown. Otherwise, the overall network Sync KPI Performance (i.e., of all network elements) will be shown.

Note: Only 'Full' syncs are considered.

</DDP_Bubble_148_ENM_Logs_Profiles_Log> <DDP_Bubble_149_PM_Mediation_ROP_Stats>

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

DDP recognizes a change in the ropStartTimeLastROP attribute as the trigger to detect when a ROP has completed, at which point it extracts the "Last" metrics as the data set for the graphs below i.e. for ROP time it displays ropEndTimeLastROP - ropStartTimeLastROP.

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.pm.collection.instrumentation.pm-service:type=FileCollectionInstrumentation

Attributes:

  • ropStartTimeLastROP: This is the time the last ROP started expressed in milliseconds since January 1st 1970.
  • ropEndTimeLastROP: This is the time the last ROP ended expressed in milliseconds since January 1st 1970.
  • numberOfFilesFailedLastROP: This is the number of files that failed in the last ROP.
  • numberOfFilesCollectedLastROP: This is the number of files that were collected successfully in the last ROP.
  • numberOfBytesTransferedLastROP: This is the number of bytes transferred in the last ROP.
  • numberOfBytesStoredLastROP: This is the number of bytes stored in the last ROP. The bytes transferred can be com pressed files to this is the uncompressed size.

Tables:

  • Duration(s): Shows the  difference between ropStartTimeLastROP and ropEndTimeLastROP for each interval.
  • Data Volume Transferred(MB): Shows numberOfBytesTransferedLastROP  / 1024 2 for each interval.
  • Files Collected: Shows numberOfFilesCollectedLastROP for each interval. 
  • Files Failed: Shows numberOfFilesCollectedLastROP for each interval.
  • Data Volume Stored(MB): Shows numberOfBytesStoredLastROP / 1024 2 for each interval.

</DDP_Bubble_149_PM_Mediation_ROP_Stats> <DDP_Bubble.pmserv.PmicRopStats>

The "ROP Stats" graphs are generated from the data collected from 'PMIC_FILE_COLLECTION_STATISTICS' log lines logged to Elasticsearch. Each 'PMIC_FILE_COLLECTION_STATISTICS' log line reports the following ROP metrics.

  • ropStartTime: The time the given ROP has started, expressed in milliseconds since January 1st 1970.
  • ropEndTime: The time the given ROP has ended, expressed in milliseconds since January 1st 1970.
  • numberOfBytesTransferred: The number of bytes transferred in the given ROP.
  • numberOfFilesCollected: The number of files successfully collected in the given ROP.
  • numberOfFilesFailed: The number of files failed in the given ROP.
  • numberOfBytesStored: The number of bytes stored in the given ROP. The bytes transferred can be compressed files. So this is the uncompressed size.


The following graphs have been generated based on the above ROP metrics.

  • Duration (s): Displays the file-collection duration (difference between 'fileCollectionStartTime' and 'ropEndTime' ) per each ROP of the given type.
                          Where  fileCollectionStartTime'  = ropIdentifier + collection delay offset + ROP interval
  • Data Volume Transferred (MB): Displays numberOfBytesTransferred/10242 for each ROP of the given type.
  • Files Collected: Displays numberOfFilesCollected for each ROP of the given type.
  • Files Failed: Displays numberOfFilesFailed for each ROP of the given type.
  • Data Volume Stored (MB): Displays numberOfBytesStored/10242 for each ROP of the given type.

</DDP_Bubble.pmserv.PmicRopStats> <DDP_Bubble_150_Profiles_Info_Log>

This table describes NHC activities.

Each row describes single NHC activity.Available information are:

  • Stop Date:date time when NHC finished processing the activity.
  • Node No: number of Network Elements from which data will be retrieved.
  • Check List: list of checks that will be performed on nodes
  • Acceptance Criteria Name: acceptance criteria name used in this activity
  • Request No: number of all tasks (Node No * Number of Checks) to collect data from the nodes.
  • Response No: number of finished tasks.
  • Report Name: report file name.

This table shows the summary of the notifications running.

For Latest ISO Version

The data collected from the following MBean:

MBean : com.ericsson.oss.mediation.cpp.notificationhandling.handlers.instrumentation.notification-receiver-handler-code-handler:type=NotificationStatsInstrumentation

For Previous ISO Version

The data is collected from the mscmserv logs of the elasticsearch data.

It displays the following attributes:

  • Received: Total Notifications Received.
  • Processed: Total Notifications Processed.
  • Discarded: Total Notifications Discarded for nodes whose sync status at the time was UNSYNCHRONIZED or PENDING.
  • Evictions: Total notifications evicted from the notifications buffer because of timeout or buffer overflow (triggers a delta sync).
  • Large Node Cache Max: Max size of the notification cache for large nodes.
  • Small Node Cache Max: Max size of the notification cache for small nodes.
  • Lead Time Max: Max of the Notification Lead Time.
  • Validation Handler Max: Max of the Notification Validation Handler Time.
  • Write Handler Max: Max of the Notification Write Handler Time.

The "All Instances" row shows the overall values for those columns. In "Max" columns it shows the overall maximum values, and in the other columns it shows the overall total values.

ddp_instr_model=[enm_mscmnotification_logs]

</DDP_Bubble.notif_analysis.processingDailyTotals> <DDP_Bubble.notif_analysis.notificationInstrumentationHelp>

For Latest ISO Version

Instrumentation Graphs are generated from the data collected from the following MBean:

MBean : com.ericsson.oss.mediation.cpp.notificationhandling.handlers.instrumentation.notification-receiver-handler-code-handler:type=NotificationStatsInstrumentation

For Previous ISO Version

Instrumentation Graphs are generated from the data collected from the mscmserv logs of the elasticsearch data.

Attributes :

  • Received: Total Notifications Received.
  • Processed: Total Notifications Processed.
  • Discarded: Total Notifications Discarded for nodes whose sync status at the time was UNSYNCHRONIZED or PENDING.
  • Lead Time Max: Max of the Notification Lead Time.
  • Small Node Cache Max: Max size of the notification cache for small nodes.
  • Large Node Cache Max: Max size of the notification cache for large nodes.
  • Evictions: Number of notifications that were evicted from notifications buffer because of timeout or buffer overflow (triggers a delta sync).
  • Validation Handler Max: Max of the Notification Validation Handler Time.
  • Write Handler Max: Max of the Notification Write Handler Time.

ddp_instr_model=[enm_mscmnotification_logs]

</DDP_Bubble.notif_analysis.notificationInstrumentationHelp> <DDP_Bubble.cm_med.notif_details>
