</DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.Failed_Amos_Commands> <DDP_Bubble_182_versant_help_bubble>

 This information is taken from JMX for the database server.

The graphs have the following information and all rates are per minute.

Data Page I/O:
db_data_reads: Pages read from sysvol + added volumes.
db_data_writes: Pages written to sysvol + added volumes.

Each page read from disk is 16KB. Versant has the notion of "extents". When a page (16KB) is loaded from disk to the Versant Server Page Cache a single 16KB page is not loaded, but always an extent. Per default one extent contains 2 pages.

Log Writes:
db_bf_llog_bytes_written: Bytes written to logical log.
db_bf_plog_bytes_written: Bytes written to physical log.

Cache Hit Ratio:
db_cache_hit_ratio db = db_data_located db / (db_data_located db + db_data_reads db).

Commits:
db_xact_committed: Transactions committed.

Rollbacks:
db_xact_rolled_back: Transactions rolled back.

Active Transactions:
db_xact_active: Active transactions.
Note: Currently the active transactions graph is not accurate due to recent changes. The progress of changes to correct this can be tracked in  this ticket 

Running Threads:
db_running_threads: Number of threads running in the backend DB.

Locks:
db_lock_timeouts: Timeouts waiting for locks.
db_lock_waits: Lock waits which occurred.


For more information see  Versant FAQ  and  Versant JPA Docs .

</DDP_Bubble_182_versant_help_bubble> <DDP_Bubble_183_enm_database_volume_information>

</DDP_Bubble_185_database_summary_info_help_message> <DDP_Bubble_186_ENM_cmserv_Activation_Details>

The CM Activation and History information  is retrieved from the ElasticSearch logs

Activation : This section holds details of the MOs activated as part of an activation job

  • Job Id : This is the unique job ID for the activation Job
  • Activation Start Time :  This is the time the activation job was started
  • Activation End Time : This is the time the activation job was finished, including the time to write history data.
  • Activation Duration :  Time in ms for the activation job to run.
  • Activation successfulChanges :  The number of MOs successfully activated
  • Activation failedChange :  The number of MOs which failed to activate
  • Activation Result :  SUCCESS - if all MOs were successfully activated, PARTIAL - if some MOs were not activated, FAILED - if none of the MOs were activated
  • Activation processedChangessPerSec :  This is the rate in MOs/second for all MOs (succcessfulChanges and failedChange)
  • Activation configName :  The name of the non live configuration which was activated.

Historical Writer :  This section holds details of MOs to be written to the CM History. Only successfully activated MOs are stored here, so if no MOs were successfully activated ( i.e. successfulChanges in the Activation section is 0, these fields will be empty .)

  • Historical Start Time:  The time that writing to the CM history store has started
  • Historical End Time: The time that writing to the CM history store has finished 
  • Historical Duration: The time in ms for writing to the CM history store
  • Historical totalMoToWrite :  The number of MOs to write to CM history store. This will never be less than sucessfulChanges, but may be higher, since some activated MOs may result in other automatic changes, e.g. automatic deletion of child MOs)
  • Historical mib_root_created :  The number of MIB Root MOs created
  • Historical mo_created :  The number of non-MIB Root MOs created
  • Historical attribute_modification :   Then umber of MOs where attributes were modified
  • Historical mo_deleted :  The number of MOs deleted, note this will include MOs automatically deleted if a parent MO is deleted.
  • Historical action_performed :  The number of MOs where an MO action is called.
  • Historical size :   The total size in bytes written to the CM History store.
  • Historical Total Written :   The total number of MOS written to the CM History store. This will equal totalMoToWrite if the storage has been completely successful, or less, if there has been some failure.
  • Historical Average size :  The average size (in bytes) of the MOs to be written to the CM history store.

NOTE : Activation Result : This field will be blank , if the "result" field is not available in the cmserv log files.

              Historical Average size :   This field will be blank , if "  Historical Total Written"    is zero

</DDP_Bubble.ecim_med.Daily_Notification_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_192_ENM_impexpserv_CM_REST_NBI_API_Daily_Summary>

This table gives an overview of the various attributes of the instrumented MBean for each instance on a daily basis.

It gives the maximum and minimum values taken by the metrics in that day for that instance.

The description of each of the metric is as below:

  • Count: It is the number of request or calls made to the Rest API.
  • RestDuration: It is the time that is taken in addition to the time actually taken by the Service to get executed. It is the execution time in MilliSeconds.
  • ServiceDuration: It is the actual execution time in MilliSeconds taken by the Service to accomplish the request or the call.
  • RestDelay: It is the time that the REST Interface adds to the time of the Service. It is in MilliSeconds. In general, equals to the difference of the RestDuration and ServiceDuration.
  • RestDelayPercentage:  It is the percentage of the delay that the REST adds to the Service.

</DDP_Bubble_192_ENM_impexpserv_CM_REST_NBI_API_Daily_Summary> <DDP_Bubble_193_ENM_impexpserv_CM_REST_NBI_API_Instr_Help>

The attributes that are stacked are: serviceDuration & restDelay .

The description of them is as below:

  • ServiceDuration: It is the actual execution time in MilliSeconds taken by the Service to accomplish the request or the call.

  • RestDelay: It is the time that the REST Interface adds to the time of the Service. It is in MilliSeconds. In general, equals to the difference of the RestDuration and ServiceDuration.


</DDP_Bubble_193_ENM_impexpserv_CM_REST_NBI_API_Instr_Help> <DDP_Bubble_194_Generic_JMX_Help>

This information is taken via JMX from various MBeans. The same information can be seen in jconsole for which there is good info here .

  • Heap committed: The amount of memory in bytes that is committed for the Java virtual machine to use. This amount of memory is guaranteed for the Java virtual machine to use.
  • Heap Used: The amount of used memory in bytes.
  • Non-Heap Committed: The current memory usage of committed non-heap memory pools that is used by the Java virtual machine.
  • Non-Heap Used: Total used for those values of all non-heap memory pools. For more info on JVM memory see here.
  • NIO Direct: Once allocated, their memory address is fixed for the lifetime of the buffer.
  • NIO Mapped: A mapped byte buffer and the file mapping that it represents remain valid until the buffer itself is garbage-collected.
    For more info on byte buffers see here .
  • Threads Current: The current number of live threads.
  • Threads Peak: The peak live thread count since the Java virtual machine started or peak was reset.
    For more info on JVM threads see here .
  • CPU Time (sec): Returns the CPU time used by the process on which the Java virtual machine is running in seconds.
  • CPU Load (%): Returns the percent CPU usage for the Java Virtual Machine process.
  • Open File Descriptors: This metric information is available for all the servers from enm ddc version:  3.20.5 and oss ddc version: R5A01. 
    This metric gives the information on the number of file descriptors kept open at that moment by the processes.
  • GC Young Generation: Total time spend in GC of young-generation space i.e. Eden and survivor. Most of the newly created objects are located here. Since most objects soon become unreachable, many objects are created in the young generation, then disappear. When objects disappear from this area, we say a "minor GC" has occurred.
  • GC Old Generation: Total time spent in GC of old generation objects. In general this type of GC has a significant impact on the process and the process is completly The objects that did not become unreachable and survived from the young generation are copied here. It is generally larger than the young generation. As it is bigger in size, the GC occurs less frequently than in the young generation. When objects disappear from the old generation, we say a "major GC" (or a "full GC") has occurred.

Note #1: Samples are taken every minute. If a sample requested for minute "n" e.g. 10:01:35 is returned in minute n+1 i.e. 10:02:05 (usuall to JVM GC) then the sample for minute n i.e. 10:01 is effctively skipped.

Note #2: During all GCs a "Stop-the-world" will occur. Stop-the-world means that the JVM is stopping the application from running to execute a GC. When stop-the-world occurs, every thread except for the threads needed for the GC will stop their tasks. The interrupted tasks will resume only after the GC task has completed. The "Stop-the-world" impact during a Young GC is not as significant as during an Old GC.

For more info on GC see Oracle Java Garbage Collection Basics and Understanding Java Garbage Collection and this from RedHat Improving OpenJDK and Oracle JDK Garbage Collection Performance..

</DDP_Bubble_194_Generic_JMX_Help> <DDP_Bubble.pki_security.EM_DT>

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.security.singlelogonservice.monitoring.single-logon-service:type=SingleLogonServiceInstrumentationBean

Attributes:

Total requests  : SUM (generateCredentialsRequests from SVC-X, listUsersRequests from SVC-X, revokeCredentialsRequests from SVC-X) per instance.

Average generate credential request time : (generateCredentialsTotalTime) / (generateCredentialsRequests) (milisec).

Average list users request time : (listUsersTotalTime) / (listUsersRequests) (milisec).

Average revoke credential request time : (revokeCredentialsTotalTime) / (revokeCredentialsRequests) (milisec).

Average generate credential PKCS12 subcall time : (credentialManagerGeneratePKCS12CredentialCallsTotalTime) / (credentialManagerGeneratePKCS12CredentialCalls) (milisec).

Average generate credential XML subcall time : (credentialManagerGenerateXMLCredentialCallsTotalTime) / (credentialManagerGenerateXMLCredentialCalls) (milisec).

Average list users subcall time : (credentialManagerListUsersTotalTime) / (listUsersRequests) (milisec).

Average revole credentials subcall time : (credentialManagerRevokeCredentialsTotalTime) / (revokeCredentialsRequests) (milisec).

Percentage share of PKI calls for generate credentials : (credentialManagerGeneratePKCS12CredentialCallsTotalTime +credentialManagerGenerateXMLCredentialCallsTotalTime) / (generateCredentialsTotalTime) * 100% (%).

Percentage share of PKI calls for list users : (credentialManagerListUsersTotalTime) / (listUsersTotalTime) * 100% (%)

</DDP_Bubble_202_ENM_Security_SingleLogonService_InstrumentationHelp> <DDP_Bubble_203_ENM_CM_Revocation_InstrumentationHelp>

The CM Revocation data is retrieved from the Elasticsearch logs. These CM Revocation values display the following information (A value of 'NA' under any given column of this table stands for "Not Available"):

  • Undo Job ID: The Id of the revocation job.

  • Start Time: The start time [hh:mm:ss] of the revocation job.

  • End Time: The end time [hh:mm:ss] of the revocation job.

  • Undo Duration: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the revocation operation.

  • Created MO: The total number of Managed Objects to be created.

  • Deleted MO: The total number of Managed Objects to be deleted.

  • Modified MO: The total number of Managed Objects to be modified.

  • Total Undo MOs: The total number of Managed Objects to be created, deleted and modified.

  • Total Operations: The total number of operations which have historical changes.

  • Unsupported Operations: The total number of operations which cannot be revoked.

  • Non NRM MOs: The total number of excluded Managed Objects due to not being in the Network Resource Model.

  • System Created MOs: The total number of excluded Managed Objects due to being System Created.

  • Not Deletable MOs: The total number of excluded Managed Objects due to being Not Deletable.

  • Total Excluded MOs: The total number of Unsupported Operations + Non NRM MOs + System Created MOs + Not Deletable MOs

  • Result: The status of the revocation job.

  • Query Time (ms): The time taken to retrieve historical data items.

  • Processing Time (ms): The time taken to process historical data items.

  • File Writing Time (ms): The time taken to write the processed historical data items.

  • Application: The application which made changes.

  • App Job ID: The job Id of the application which made changes.

</DDP_Bubble_203_ENM_CM_Revocation_InstrumentationHelp> <DDP_Bubble_205_ENM_VCS_Event_Details>

The information is based on VCS resource and group information taken from the VCS engine log files.

Resource related:

  • MonitorOffline: The VCS resource monitor script has found that the resource is offline.
  • MonitorTimeout: The VCS resource monitor script did not complete within the configured time.
  • CleanStart: VCS has started to execute the clean script on the resource. Clean is normally called if offline or online do not complete with the the expected time or after the number of MonitorTimeouts has reached the configured ToleranceLimit.
  • CleanCompleted: The VCS clean script has completed execution.
  • RestartStart: VCS has initiated a restart of the resource (usually after the resource has become offline unexpectedly).
  • RestartCompleted: The VCS resource restart is completed.
  • OnlineStart: VCS has initiated an online of the resource.
  • OnlineCompleted: The VCS resource online has completed.
  • OfflineStart: VCS has initiated an offline of the resource.
  • OfflineCompleted: The VCS resource offline has completed.
  • Faulted: The VCS resource is Faulted.

Downtime: The downtime for a given resource is calculated as below and showed against OnlineCompleted and RestartCompleted events. The downtime will be presented as 'NA' (Not Applicable) against resource events other than OnlineCompleted and RestartCompleted.

    • Downtime = (OnlineCompleted time - Latest OfflineCompleted time prior to this OnlineCompleted event)
      Note: If there is no OfflineCompleted event (corresponding to the given OnlineCompleted event) found today and yesterday then the downtime will be shown as 'NOCEF' (No OfflineCompleted Event Found) under the table.
    • Downtime = (RestartCompleted time - Latest CleanCompleted time prior to this RestartCompleted event)
      Note: If there is no CleanCompleted event (corresponding to the given RestartCompleted event) found today and yesterday then the downtime will be shown as 'NCCEF' (No CleanCompleted Event Found) under the table.

OnlineTime: The onlinetime for a given resource is calculated as below and showed against OnlineCompleted and O nlineStart events. The downtime will be presented as 'NA' (Not Applicable) against resource events other than OnlineCompleted and O nlineStart .

    • OnlineTime = (OnlineCompleted time - Latest OnlineStart time prior to this  OnlineCompleted event)
      Note: If there is no OnlineStart event (corresponding to the given OnlineCompleted event) found today and yesterday then the downtime will be shown as 'NOCEF' (No OnlineStart Event Found) under the table.

System related:

  • Command: freeze persistent evacuate: VCS has initiated an evacuation of all groups from this node. This normally indicates the start of a rolling upgrade of that node.
  • Command: unfreeze persistent: VCS unfreezes the node which means that the node can online groups if required to do so. This normally indicates the end of a rolling upgrade of that node.

For more information see the LITP model here and here and the VCS documentation here.

</DDP_Bubble_205_ENM_VCS_Event_Details> <DDP_Bubble_206_ENM_VCS_Resource_Downtime_Totals>

The table presents the downtime statistics observed for various VCS resources on the given day. The information is based on VCS resource and group information taken from the VCS engine log files.

  • Outage Count: The number of outages observed for the given resource on the given day.
  • Total Downtime: The sum (HH:MM:SS) of all the downtimes observed for the given resource and represents the total time for which that resource is down on the given day.

</DDP_Bubble_218_ENM_Monthly_Server_Elastic_FS_Used> <DDP_Bubble_219_ENM_impexpserv_CM_REST_NBI_API_Daily_Summary>

This table gives an overview of the various attributes of the instrumented MBean for each instance on a daily basis.

It gives the maximum,average and minimum values taken by the metrics in that day for all the instances.

The description of each of the metric is as below:

  • Count: It is the total number of request or calls made to the Rest API.
  • RestDuration: It is the time that is taken in addition to the time actually taken by the Service to get executed. It is the execution time in MilliSeconds.
  • ServiceDuration: It is the actual execution time in MilliSeconds taken by the Service to accomplish the request or the call.
  • RestDelay: It is the time that the REST Interface adds to the time of the Service. It is in MilliSeconds. In general, equals to the difference of the RestDuration and ServiceDuration.

The CM Config Copy data is retrieved from the ElasticSearch logs. These CM Config Copy values display the following information:

  • Job Id: The job id number
  • Status: Indicates whether the copy job has been successfully or unsuccessfully completed
  • Start Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the copy started
  • End Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the copy completed
  • Total Elapsed Time: The total time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the copy job
  • Expected Nodes Copied: The number of nodes that are expected to be copied
  • Nodes Copied: The number of nodes successfully copied
  • Nodes Not Copied: The number of nodes unsuccessfully copied
  • Nodes No Match Found: The number of nodes where no match has been found
  • Source Config: The config that the nodes were copied from
  • Target Config: The config that the nodes were copied to

This 'Daily Total' values display the following information:

  • Method Invocations (SCR POST): The total number of CLI SCR submitCommand() method invocations on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SCR POST): The average execution time (in millisec) per invocation of CLI SCR submitCommand() on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SFD POST): The average execution time (in millisec) per invocation of CLI SFD addCommand() on the given day.
  • Method Invocations (SCR HEAD): The total number of CLI SCR getCommandStatusForRequest() method invocations on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SCR HEAD): The average execution time (in millisec) per invocation of CLI SCR getCommandStatusForRequest() on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SFD HEAD): The average execution time (in millisec) per invocation of CLI SFD getCommandStatus() on the given day.
  • Method Invocations (SCR GETS): The combined total number of CLI SCR getTerminalCommandOutput() , CLI SCR getTerminalTextOutput() & CLI SCR getObjectCommandOutput() method invocations on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SCR GETS): The average execution time(in millisec) per combined invocation of CLI SCR getTerminalCommandOutput() , CLI SCR getTerminalTextOutput() & CLI SCR getObjectCommandOutput() on the given day.
  • Avg Execution Time (SFD GETS): The average execution time (in millisec) per invocation of CLI SFD getCommandResponse() on the given day.

The "Combined File Collection Instrumentation" graphs are generated from the data collected from the following MBean:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.pm.collection.instrumentation.pm-service:type=FileCollectionStatistics

MBean Attributes:

  • combinedNumberOfTransferredBytes: The number of bytes transferred, for both 1-min and 15-min ROPs combined, for the given interval.
  • combinedNumberOfFilesCollected: The number of files collected, for both 1-min and 15-min ROPs combined, for the given interval.
  • combinedNumberOfFilesFailed: The number of files failed, for both 1-min and 15-min ROPs combined, for the given interval.
  • combinedNumberOfStoredBytes: The number of bytes stored, for both 1-min and 15-min ROPs combined, for the given interval.

Combined File Collection Instrumentation Graphs:

  • Data Volume Transferred (MB): Displays combinedNumberOfTransferredBytes/10242 for each interval.
  • Files Collected: Displays combinedNumberOfFilesCollected for each interval.
  • Files Failed: Displays combinedNumberOfFilesFailed for each interval.
  • Data Volume Stored (MB): Displays combinedNumberOfStoredBytes/10242 for each interval.

</DDP_Bubble.pmserv.combinedFileCollectionInstr> <DDP_Bubble.pm_med.PmicRopDailyTotals>

The "Daily Totals" information is obtained from 'PMIC_FILE_COLLECTION_STATISTICS' log lines logged to Elasticsearch.

  • Avg Duration (s): The average file-collection duration per ROP of the given type for the given day.
  • Max Duration (s): The maximum file-collection duration per ROP of the given type for the given day.
  • Files Collected: The total number of files collected for all ROPs of the given type on the given day.
  • Files Failed: The total number of files failed for all ROPs of the given type on the given day.
  • GB Transferred: The total number of GB transferred for all ROPs of the given type on the given day.
  • GB Stored: The total number of GB stored for all ROPs of the given type on the given day.

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PULL") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Whethere a node is push or pull is determined by fileCollectionCategories.txt provided by PM. Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:35 and hh:50 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

</DDP_Bubble.pm_med.PmicRopDailyTotals> <DDP_Bubble.pm_med.flsROPHelp>

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PULL") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Whethere a node is push or pull is determined by fileCollectionCategories.txt provided by PM. Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:35 and hh:50 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

Memory information is retrieved using the "sar -A" command.

Solaris Notes:

The free ram graph on a Solaris system represents the amount of memory available to processes.

Linux Notes:

Free memory is memory not currently used by applications, in buffers or cached.

Used memory includes kernel memory which can sometimes incorporate large sections for inode_cache and dentry. These can be seen with  cat /proc/slabinfo and  cat /proc/meminfo.

</DDP_Bubble.enm_amos.AMOS_Processes> <DDP_Bubble_239_ENM_ElasticSearch_Stats_Indices>

Indices level stats provide statistics on different operations happening on an index.

The below set of graphs provide information regarding the indices of the elasticsearch Service.

All these information is available in the elasticsearch.stats file with the tag "indices":

Query Count: It indicates the number of the queries for searching the information

Query Average Time: It indicates the average time taken for the queries ran.

Fetch Count: It indicates the count of the data that is being fetched

Fetch Average Time: It indicates the average time taken for the fetch data

Index Count: It indicates the count for the indexing

Index Average Time: It indicates the average time for indexing

Store Size in MB: Amount of data stored in MB

Docs Deleted: The number of docs / deleted docs (docs not yet merged out). Note, this value in general is affected by refreshing the index. 

It is considered as a running total while representing the graphs.

</DDP_Bubble_239_ENM_ElasticSearch_Stats_Indices> <DDP_Bubble_240_ENM_ElasticSearch_Stats_Threadpools>

A node holds several thread pools in order to improve how threads memory consumption are managed within a node. Many of these pools also have queues associated with them, which allow pending requests to be held instead of discarded.

This table provides the statistics about the various threadpools and their statuses which is taken from the elasticsearch.stats file with the tag " thread_pool".


The thread pools shown are:

Index: For index/delete operations.

Search: For count/search/suggest operations

Management: Thread pool used for management of Elasticsearch (e.g. cluster management)

Listener: Mainly for java client executing of action when listener threaded is set to true

Generic: For generic operations (e.g., background node discovery)

Flush: Thread pool used for flush operations

Warmer: For segment warm-up operations.

Refresh: For refresh operations.


The pool details are:

Thread Pool: Name or category of the thread pool

Total Completed:Number of the completed threads

Total Rejected: Number of the rejected threads

Max Active: Maximum number of active threads in the thread pool

Max Queue: Maximum number of the threads under queue in the thread pool


For more information see here.


</DDP_Bubble_240_ENM_ElasticSearch_Stats_Threadpools> <DDP_Bubble_241_ENM_Workload_Profiles_Graph>

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.services.topologyCollectionsService.service.instrumentation.topologyCollectionsService:type=InstrumentationBean

Attributes:

  • collectionTotalTime  : Total time to retrieve collections (only collection object)
  • collectionDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to retrieve the collection PO from database
  • collectionWithContentsTotalTime  : Total time to retrieve a collection with contents
  • collectionWithContentsDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to retrieve collection contents from the database
  • createCollectionTotalTime  : Total time to create a collection
  • createCollectionDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to create a collection in database
  • updateCollectionTotalTime  : Total time to update a collection
  • updateCollectionDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to update a collection in database
  • deleteCollectionTotalTime  : Total time to delete a collection
  • deleteCollectionDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to delete a collection in database
  • collectionBatchesTotalTime  : Total time to process each collection batch (when reading collection contents)
  • autoGeneratedCollectionsCount : The number of auto generated collections
  • publicCollectionsCount : The number of public collections
  • privateCollectionsCount : The number of private collections
  • createCollectionDatabaseLargestSize : The size of the largest collection
  • createCollectionDatabaseAverageSize : The average size of all collections
  • createCollectionDatabaseMedianSize : The median size of all collections
  • createCollectionDatabaseTotalObjectCount : The total number of MOs in all collections


  • savedSearchesTotalTime  : Total time to retrive a saved search object (don't include search execution)
  • savedSearchesDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to retrive a saved search object from the database
  • createSavedSearchTotalTime  : Total time to create a saved search
  • createSavedSearchDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to create a saved search in the database
  • deleteSavedSearchTotalTime  : Total time to delete a saved search
  • deleteSavedSearchDatabaseTotalTime  : Total time to delete a saved search from the database
  • publicSavedSearchesCount : The number of public saved searches
  • privateSavedSearchesCount : The number of private saved searches

This table shows which services are used by which applications. Each application tags it's REST call with an "application name" and that is the application name shown in the table. The "request" column is the total number of service calls made by that application.

</DDP_Bubble_276_ENM_Apache_Totals_Application_UI> <DDP_Bubble_278_ENM_Jboss_Threadpools_Help>

The Thread Pool Status data set contains information that reflects the status of the internal thread pool used to collect data. Thresholds for this data set are associated with the JBoss component.

MBean: threadpool-<name>

<name> can be default, async, workmanager_short, workmanager_long, http_executor,ajp_executor or job_executor_tp.

For EAP7, threadpool names are io_http_executor, io_https_executor, io_ajp_executor

Attributes:

  • completedTaskCount (COMPLETEDTASKCOUNT): The approximate total number of tasks that have completed execution. The type is integer (32-bit gauge).
  • activeCount (ACTIVECOUNT): The approximate number of threads that are running tasks actively. The type is integer (32-bit gauge).
  • queueSize (QUEUESIZE): The size of the queue. The type is integer (32-bit gauge).
  • rejectedCount (REJECTEDCOUNT): The number of tasks that are rejected. The type is integer (32-bit gauge).
  • currentThreadCount(CURRENTTHREADCOUNT): The approximate number of threads that are running tasks actively.
  • busyThreadCount: The number of threads that are busy in running activities

Note: For some threads like default and sync, both activeCount and currentThreadCount are present and for few threads like http, ajp, workmanager,jon_executor_tp.. only currentThreadCount with similar description are available.

</DDP_Bubble_278_ENM_Jboss_Threadpools_Help> <DDP_Bubble_279_ENM_Cell_Counts_Help>

The table is populated with the data resulting from DB queries.

Note: If the "Total Count" column is displayed, then it includes all MOs from both the "live" and "non-live" buckets.

Currently, this table is displayed for the MOs - 'EUtranCellFDD', 'EUtranCellTDD', 'NbIotCell', 'GeranCell', 'NodeBLocalCell', 'RbsLocalCell' and 'NRCellDU'.

'NbIotCell' cells are considered as 1/13th of a cell (as per CA analysis) for capacity reasons and are rounded up to the nearest whole number.

EUtranCells can be calculated to be the sum of RbsLocalCell and NodeBLocalCell or the total can be seen in the MO Count page in the database analysis page.

</DDP_Bubble_281_ENM_Versant_Clients_Stats_Help> <DDP_Bubble.cm_imports.Daily_Totals>

The Bulk CM Import Daily Totals data is retrieved from the Elasticsearch logs. NA is used for fields which are null or not provided in Elasticsearch. These Bulk CM Import Daily Totals values display the following information:

  • Jobs: The amount of import jobs with this particular status
  • Status: The status of these import jobs.
  • File Format: The format of the file used for the import job.
  • Configuration: The name of the configuration used for the import job.
  • Copy Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the copy operation.
  • Parsing Time: Total Parsing time for the import jobs of this status.
  • Import Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import operation.
  • Total Elapsed Time: The total time [hh:mm:ss] taken to complete the import job (i.e., the time elapsed between 'Copy Start' and 'Import End').
  • Nodes Copied: The total number of nodes copied as part of the import job.
  • Nodes Not Copied: The total number of nodes not copied as part of the import job.
  • MOs Created: The total number of Managed Objects created.
  • MOs Updated: The total number of Managed Objects updated.
  • MOs Deleted: The total number of Managed Objects deleted.
  • Avg MOs Processed Per Sec: The Average number of Managed Objects (MOs) imported per second
  • Max MOs Processed Per Sec: The Maximum number of Managed Objects (MOs) imported per second
  • Min MOs Processed Per Sec: The Minimum number of Managed Objects (MOs) imported per second

</DDP_Bubble.cm_imports.Daily_Totals> <DDP_Bubble.cm_exports.Daily_Totals>

The Bulk CM Export Daily Totals data is retrieved from the ElasticSearch logs. These Bulk CM Export Daily Totals values display the following information:

  • Total Jobs: Total number of jobs grouped by Type,Status,Filter
  • Max Duration: Maximum timedifference of jobs end_date_time and start_date_time
  • Status: Indicates whether the export job has been successfully or unsuccessfully completed
  • Filter: Filter type used in the export job
  • Total MOs: The total number of MOs exported
  • Max MOs per sec: The Maximum number of Managed Objects (MOs) exported per second
  • Min MOs per sec: The Minimum number of Managed Objects (MOs) exported per second
  • Avg MOs per sec: The Average number of Managed Objects (MOs) exported per second
  • Type: The MO type
  • Nodes Expected: Total number of nodes that are expected to be exported
  • Nodes Exported: Total number of nodes that are succesfully exported
  • Nodes Not Exported: Total number of nodes that are unsuccesfully exported
  • Nodes No Match Found: Total number of nodes where no match has been found

</DDP_Bubble.autoid.MO_Details_Table> <DDP_Bubble_307_FM_NBI_Notifications>

An event is an FM entity that has no state i.e. it is only raised by the sender.

An alarm is an FM entity that has state i.e. it can be raised and cleared by the sender.

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.nbi.fm.corba.instrumentation.corbaserver:type=NBIInstrumentationBean

Attributes:

  • eventsPresentInNotificationsList: Number of events that are present at the CORBA NBI.
  • alarmsPresentInNotificationsList: Number of alarms that are present at the CORBA NBI.
  • eventsSentToNotificationService: Number of events that are sent to the NMS from the CORBA NBI.
  • alarmsSentToNotificationService: Number of alarms that are sent to the NMS from the CORBA NBI.
  • eventsReceivedfromCorbaserverQueue: Number of events that are received by CORBA NBI.
  • eventsReceivedfromFmNorthBoundQueue: Number of events that are received by FM North Bound.
  • alarmsReceivedfromCorbaserverQueue: Number of alarms that are received by the CORBA NBI.
  • alarmsReceivedfromFmNorthBoundQueue: Number of alarms that are received by the FM North Bound.
  • activeNMSSubscriptionsCount: Number of Active NMS Subscriptions towards FM NBI.
  • alarmLatency: The total time(in seconds) time taken for an alarm to reach FM NBI from FM Mediation.
  • failedAlarmsCount: Total number of Failed Alarm.

Note:
- Total number of NMS subscriptions : All the subscriptions are shown on only the master instance. However, actual subscriptions are shared among all the available nbalarmirp instances.
- Average Latency : It is the average latency of alarms processed in each minute by that instance of nbalarmirp, obtained by 'alarmLatency / latencyAlarmCount'

</DDP_Bubble_307_FM_NBI_Notifications> <DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Daily_Notification_Totals>

    ExchangesCompleted : This is the total number of notifications processed in an instance.

Below data is collected from instrumentation Logs from MBean com.ericsson.oss.itpf.modeling.modelservice:type=ModelServiceCache

  • Cache Size: The number of entries in the cache. A model may have more than one entry in the cache, with the different entries being applicable to different target types.
  • Cache Misses: The number of requests that required external retrieval of a model as opposed to read directly from the cache.
  • Cache Requests: The total number of requests that are made to retrieve a model.
  • Model Count: The number of models in the cache.
  • Cache Hit %: (numberOfCacheRequests -numberOfCacheMisses)/numberOfCacheRequests * 100)
  • Cache Description Texts:  Property describing if description texts within models are to be replaced with empty strings or not. The default is {@code ALL} (indicated by the value zero) meaning that by default all description texts are cached. {@code NONE} (indicated by the value of one) is the only other valid value; in this case model description texts will be replaced by empty strings.
  • Max Cache Idletime (sec): The amount of time (in seconds) an entry in the cache can be idle before eviction. The default is -1 and is interpreted as unlimited lifespan within the cache.
  • Max Cache size (Total):  The maximum number of entries allowed in the model service cache. A value of zero indicates that cache eviction is not enabled and therefore an unlimited amount of entries is allowed
  • Cache Evictions (Total):  The number of models evicted from the cache.
  • ReadWriteRatio (Ratio):  The read/write ratio of the cache. The value displayed is rounded to the nearest whole number.

ddp_instr_model=[TOR/common/enm_shmmodeling_instr]

</DDP_Bubble.modelling.modeling_stats> <DDP_Bubble_310_SHMCORESERV_Job_Execution_Flow>

Below graphs provides information about job Execution of :

  • Upgrade Activity for CPP nodes
  • Activate Activity for ECIM nodes
  • Restore activities for CPP and ECIM nodes.
  • Create Backup activity for ECIM nodes

  • Upload Backup activities for CPP and ECIM nodes

There are three flows,through which a job can be completed:

  • Through Notifications
  • Through Polling
  • Through Timeout

The graph will display the number of nodes on which the respective activity is completed through notifications/polling/timeout.

</DDP_Bubble_329_AddSupport_Node_Versions> <DDP_Bubble_330_server_daily_average>

The table presents the daily average CPU usage, while the graph presents the CPU load across the day. The metrics presented are retrieved using the command

sar -A

The following metrics are presented:

  • Usr+Guest: the percentage of CPU time spent executing application code.
  • Sys: the percentage of CPU time spent executing system calls in the kernel.

  • IO Wait: purported to be the percentage of time spent waiting for IO. In reality this is a pretty useless metric as it is difficult for the kernel to calculate accurately, and since Solaris 10 this is always 0.

  • Steal: Percentage of time spent in involuntary wait by the virtual CPU or CPUs while the hypervisor was servicing another virtual processor.
  • Total: the total percentage of CPU time spent doing stuff - i.e. %Usr + %Guest + %Sys + %IO Wait + %Steal.

</DDP_Bubble.ecim_med.notif_top_details> <DDP_Bubble_336_ENM_CM_MEDIATION_SyncStats>

The below table contains the details about fetched Network Element.

  • Duration: Duration of sync in milliseconds from when the sync was initiated in the flow
  • MOs: Total MOs synced
  • Attributes: Total attributes synced
  • MO/sec: Rate of MOs synced per second: (Total MOs synced)/(Total duration for sync)
  • Adjusted MO/sec: Rate of MOs synced per second using DPS time only: (Total MOs synced)/(DPS topology duration + DPS attribute duration). The goal of this derived metric is to remove the network/node f rom the sync performance metric as much as possible so as to better gauge of internal sync performance
  • NE Tolology: Time taken for the network element (NE) topology handler to get the topology from the NE
  • DPS Topology: Time taken for DPS topology handler to write the topology to the database. This includes the addition and deletion of MOs on the database to reflect the NE topology
  • NE Attribute: Time taken for the NE attribute handler to get the attributes from the NE
  • DPS Attribute: Time taken for DPS attribute handler to write the attributes to the database

For DELTA Syncs, some of the columns have different meanings:

  • NE Tolology: Time taken for the network element info handler to get info from the NE
  • NE Attribute: Time taken to read the changes from the NE
  • DPS Topology: Time taken to merge the changes
  • DPS Attribute: Time taken to write the changes to DPS
  • MOs Created: MOs created or updated
  • MOs Deleted: MOs deleted

</DDP_Bubble_336_ENM_CM_MEDIATION_SyncStats> <DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Sync_Analysis>

Shows the details of requested Node element.

</DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Sync_Analysis> <DDP_Bubble_338_BUR_Backup_Throughput_Daily_Totals>

The Backup (BUR) throughput details are retrieved from 'measurement_backup_FilesystemThroughput.data' logs. The 'Daily Totals' table displays the following information:

  • Start Time: The start time of the earliest filesytem-backup among all the hosts for the given backup.
  • End Time: The end time of the filesystem back that finished last among all the hosts for the given backup.
  • Backup: The keyword of the given backup.
  • Overall Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under all the hosts with the total time (in sec) taken for all those filesystem-backups under all those hosts.
  • Overall Parallel Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under all the hosts with the time difference between the start time of the earliest filesystem-backup (among all the hosts) and the end time of the latest filesystem-backup (among all the hosts). Note: The 'Overall Parallel Throughput' generally tends to be larger than 'Overall Throughput' since the time used to calculate the former spans multiple filesystem-backups running in parallel.
  • Num of Filesystems: The total number of filesystems that have been backed-up across all the hosts of ENM.
  • Total Size (MB): The total size of the data that has been backed-up across all the filesystems and hosts of ENM.

Note:  SFS backup details are displayed in the below tables separately

</DDP_Bubble_338_BUR_Backup_Throughput_Daily_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_339_CCPCM_Mediation_Sync_KPI_Performance>

  • Sync Times By Stage:Graph represents the 4 attributes(NE Topology,DPS Topology,NE Attribute,DPS Attribute) with the X axis being sync start time.
  • Sync Duration:Graph represents duration with the X axis being sync start time
  • Sync Rate:Graph represents MOs/sec attribute with the X axis being sync start time.

</DDP_Bubble_339_CCPCM_Mediation_Sync_KPI_Performance> <DDP_Bubble_340_BUR_Backup_Throughput_Details>

The Backup (BUR) throughput details are retrieved from 'measurement_backup_FilesystemThroughput.data' logs. The 'Throughput Details' table displays the following information:

  • Start Time: The start time of the backup operation for the given filesystem under the given host.
  • End Time: The end time of the backup operation for the given filesystem under the given host.
  • Backup: The keyword of the given backup.
  • Host: The hostname of the server whose filesystem is getting backed-up.
  • Throughput (MB/sec): The throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for the given filesystem under the given host with the total time (in sec) taken for that backup operation (i.e., difference between the start and end times).
  • Backup Mount Point: The path to backup mount point.
  • Filesystem: The filesystem that is getting backed-up.
  • Filesystem Used Size (MB): The size of data available under the filesystem at the time of backup.
  • Filesystem Total Size (MB): The total size of the filesystem.

</DDP_Bubble_348_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_IOPS_V2> <DDP_Bubble.neo4j.transactions>

Metrics for below graphs is displayed from either neo4j 3.x or 4.x

3.x Metrics

Below graph data is taken from JMX of the Neo4j VMs via the MBean  'org.neo4j:instance=kernel#0,name=Transactions'   . The information is presented under the following graphs:

  • Open:  The number of currently open transactions at that instant in time. (value of NumberOfOpenTransactions).
  • Opened:  The number of started transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfOpenedTransactions)
  • Committed:  The number of committed transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfCommittedTransactions)
  • RolledBack:  The number of rolled back transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfRolledBackTransactions)

4.x Metrics

This information is taken from JMX of the Neo4j VMs via below MBeans The information is presented under the following graphs:

MBean:  neo4j-NumberOfOpenTransaction

  • Attribute: Value -  The number of currently open transactions at that instant in time. (value of NumberOfOpenTransactions).

MBean: neo4j-NumberOfOpenedTransactions

  • Attribute: Count - The number of started transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfOpenedTransactions)

MBean: neo4j-NumberOfCommittedTransactions

  • Attribute: Count - The number of committed transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfCommittedTransactions)

MBean: neo4j-NumberOfRollbackTransactions

  • Attribute: Count - The number of rolled back transactions since the previous sample period. (delta of NumberOfRolledBackTransactions)


Note: For Opened, Committed & RolledBack, when the value is "x" at time T it means that "x" transactions were Opened, Committed or RolledBack between time T and the previous sample which is usually 1 minute before.

</DDP_Bubble.neo4j.transactions> <DDP_Bubble.neo4j.pagecache>

This information is taken from JMX of the Neo4j for 3.x or 4.x versions

3.x

MBean:  ' org.neo4j:instance=kernel#0,name=Page cache'


4.x

MBeans:

neo4j-BytesRead

neo4j-BytesWritten

neo4j-EvictionExceptions

neo4j-Evictions

neo4j-Faults

neo4j-Flushes

neo4j-Pins


Attributes:

  • Count 

KbRead: The number of bytes read (in KB) from durable storage.

KbWritten: The number of bytes written (in KB) to durable storage.

Evictions: The number of page evictions i.e., the number of pages removed from the memory to make room for other pages.

EvictionExceptions: The number of exceptions caught during page eviction. Note: This should ideally be zero or at least not increasing. Otherwise it may indicate a drive failure [OR] storage space or permission problems.

Faults: The number of page faults. It indicates the frequency of the requested data being not found in memory and has to be loaded.

Flushes: The number of page flushes. It represents the dirty pages that have been written to durable storage.

Pins: The number of page pins. It represents the number of pages have been accessed.

For general information on JMX for Neo see Developer reference - Chapter 9.

</DDP_Bubble.neo4j.pagecache> <DDP_Bubble.cm_med.Route_Instrumentation>

</DDP_Bubble_365_Read_Cell_Management> <DDP_Bubble_366_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_CPU_Usage>

The graph displays the sum of CPU time (in minutes) of all the VMs at one minute intervals. The 'CPU Time (in minutes)' is derived from the 'CPU (%)' stats of 'sar' data as 'cpu_time_min = ((cpu_percentage/100) x number_of_processors)' .

The 'CPU Time' displayed here comprises of 'Usr' + 'Sys' + 'Guest' components.

Note: At the moment, the 'IO Wait' component is not part of the 'CPU Time' shown under this graph. For 'IO Wait' statistics, please refer to the 'CPU' graph under the 'server' page of the respective hosts.

</DDP_Bubble_366_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_CPU_Usage> <DDP_Bubble_367_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_CPU_Steal>

The graph displays the sum of CPU steal (in minutes) of all the VMs at one minute intervals. The 'CPU Steal (in minutes)' is derived from the 'Steal (%)' stats of 'sar' data as 'cpu_steal_min = ((steal_percentage/100) x number_of_processors)' .

</DDP_Bubble_367_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_CPU_Steal> <DDP_Bubble_368_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_Memory_Usage>

The graph displays the sum of memory usage (in MB) of all the VMs at one minute intervals. These 'Memory Usage (in MB)' stats are obtained from 'sar' data and comprises of 'Used' + 'Buffers' + 'Cached' components.

</DDP_Bubble_368_Resource_Usage_Summary_VM_Memory_Usage> <DDP_Bubble_369_Resource_Usage_Summary_PM_15MIN_ROP_Duration>

The "PM 15MIN ROP Duration" graph is generated from the data collected from 'PMIC_FILE_COLLECTION_STATISTICS' log lines logged to Elasticsearch. The graph displays the file-collection duration (difference between 'fileCollectionStartTime' and 'ropEndTime' ) per each 15MIN ROP.

Where  fileCollectionStartTime'  = ropIdentifier + collection delay offset + ROP interval

</DDP_Bubble_369_Resource_Usage_Summary_PM_15MIN_ROP_Duration> <DDP_Bubble_370_ENM_PM_Snmp_Totals>

The information displayed in the below table and the graph contains the data collected from the instrumented beans.

MBean: com.ericsson.oss.mediation.pm.service.instrumentation.snmp-pm-engine:type=SnmpPmEngineInstrumentationBean of the service group: mspmip.

Attributes:

  • snmpGetNumberOperation: It is the number of snmp operations performed. It is measured in Units.
  • snmpGetDurationTime: It is the time taken to get the values of counters. It is measured in MilliSeconds.
  • snmpGetSizeResponseMessage: It is the size of the response message from the snmp. It is measured in Bytes.

Of these, snmpGetNumberOperation is a running total attribute while the other two metrics displayed in the table are of absolute nature.

</DDP_Bubble_370_ENM_PM_Snmp_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_371_ENM_PM_File_Generated_Totals>

  • fileGeneratedTime: It is the total time taken to create a pm file. It is measured in MilliSeconds.

</DDP_Bubble_378_ESXi_CPU> <DDP_Bubble_379_vENM_Workflow_Logs>

The table presents the workflow details parsed out of the raw 'workflows.log' file collected by DDC.

  • Workflow: The business key ('businessKey') of the given workflow.
  • Definition Name: The definition name ('definitionName') of the given workflow.
  • Start Time: The start time ('startTime') of the given workflow.
  • End Time: The end time ('endTime') of the given workflow.
  • Duration: The time taken by the given workflow calculated as the time elapsed between 'startTime' and 'endTime'.
  • Aborted: The 'aborted' status of the given workflow.
  • Log Message: The log message ('log') of the given workflow.

Note: If the 'Log Message' has too many log messages to display under the table then only first few messages are shown in the table cell with a link at the end. Clicking the link should take us to a new page with the full 'Log Message' for that particular workflow log.

</DDP_Bubble_379_vENM_Workflow_Logs> <DDP_Bubble_380_vENM_Workflow_Log_Details>

  • Workflow: The business key ('businessKey') of the given workflow.
  • Definition Name: The definition name ('definitionName') of the given workflow.
  • Start Time: The start time ('startTime') of the given workflow.
  • End Time: The end time ('endTime') of the given workflow.
  • Duration: The time taken by the given workflow calculated as the time elapsed between 'startTime' and 'endTime'.
  • Aborted: The 'aborted' status of the given workflow.

</DDP_Bubble_380_vENM_Workflow_Log_Details> <DDP_Bubble_381_vENM_Workflow_Log_Message>

</DDP_Bubble_381_vENM_Workflow_Log_Message> <DDP_Bubble_382_vENM_Consul_N_SAM_Events>

The data has been retrieved from the below logs that have been logged to Elasticsearch.

  • The Consul and SAM logs of 'serviceregistry' VMs
  • The HADley logs of all VMs

The table consists of the following fields.

  • Time: The time of the given Consul/SAM log.
  • Type: The program from which the log has originated.
  • Member: The hostname of the given member.
  • Message: The concise keyword representing one of the following logs:
    1. HcFailed: <health_check_script_name> - A message from HADley reporting a failed health check script.
    2. MemberFailed_HealthCritical - A message from Consul reporting that the given member failed and its health has been marked as 'critical'.
    3. MemberFailed_VnfLafNotified - A message from SAM that VNF-LAF is being notified about the given failed member.
    4. MemberLeft_Deregistering - A message from Consul reporting that the given member left and its services are getting deregistered.
    5. MemberJoined_HealthAlive - A message from Consul reporting that the given member joined the cluster and its health has been marked as 'alive'.

For more informtion on HA of ENM in the cloud see here.

</DDP_Bubble_382_vENM_Consul_N_SAM_Events> <DDP_Bubble.ecim_med.fullsynctotals>

  • Avg Duration: The average duration time [hh:mm:ss] of syncs on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Avg MOs/Sec: The average number of Managed Objects per second synced on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals

  • Total MOs Parsed: The total number of Managed Objects parsed on the specified Instance or the total parsed across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Total MOs Created: The total number of Managed Objects created on the specified Instance or the total created across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Total MOs Updated: The total number of Managed Objects updated on the specified Instance or the total updated across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Total MOs Deleted: The total number of Managed Objects deleted on the specified Instance or the total deleted across all Instances where Instance equals Totals

</DDP_Bubble.net_log_stats.Netlog_Counters_Summary> <DDP_Bubble_405_Gen_JMX_Total_GC_Time>

This information is taken via JMX from various MBeans. The same information can be seen in jconsole for which there is good info here .

  • GC Young Generation: Total time spend in GC of young-generation space i.e. Eden and survivor. Most of the newly created objects are located here. Since most objects soon become unreachable, many objects are created in the young generation, then disappear. When objects disappear from this area, we say a "minor GC" has occurred.
  • GC Old Generation: Total time spent in GC of old generation objects. In general this type of GC has a significant impact on the process and the process is completly The objects that did not become unreachable and survived from the young generation are copied here. It is generally larger than the young generation. As it is bigger in size, the GC occurs less frequently than in the young generation. When objects disappear from the old generation, we say a "major GC" (or a "full GC") has occurred.

Note: During all GCs a "Stop-the-world" will occur. Stop-the-world means that the JVM is stopping the application from running to execute a GC. When stop-the-world occurs, every thread except for the threads needed for the GC will stop their tasks. The interrupted tasks will resume only after the GC task has completed. The "Stop-the-world" impact during a Young GC is not as significant as during an Old GC.

</DDP_Bubble_405_Gen_JMX_Total_GC_Time> <DDP_Bubble.net_log_stats.Shared_Netlog_Mediation_Handler>

Instrumentation graphs are generated from data collected from the following MBean:

  • com.ericsson.oss.mediation.netlog.instrumentation.shared-netlog-pull-mediation-handler:type=SharedNetlogPullStatistics

Attributes:

  • MSNETLOG Instance: The instance number of the MSNETLOG cluster.
  • Mediation Task Request received: The number of Mediaiton Task Request received.
  • Upload started: The number of collection started.
  • Execution time:  Running time of the last collection.

</DDP_Bubble_412_APSERV_HARDWARE_REPLACE_EXEC_TIMES> <DDP_Bubble_413_ENM_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_Purpose>

The goal of this page is to show the analysis of ENM resource usage over the last 10 days.

The expectation is that these usage patterns will be somewhat predictable and inter-related, so when all are considered together, it may help to understand the capacity, performance and availability of the underlying resources.

</DDP_Bubble_413_ENM_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_Purpose> <DDP_Bubble_414_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_IOPS>

The graph displays the sum of the maximum IOPS (Input/output Operations Per Second) of all the VMs (on y-axis) for every 15 Min interval (on x-axis) for the last 10 days.

</DDP_Bubble_414_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_IOPS> <DDP_Bubble_415_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_CPU_Usage>

The graph displays the sum of the maximum CPU times (in minutes) of all the VMs (on y-axis) for every 15 Min interval (on x-axis) for the last 10 days.

The 'CPU Time (in minutes)' is derived from the 'CPU (%)' stats of 'sar' data as 'cpu_time_min = ((cpu_percentage/100) x number_of_processors)' . The 'CPU Time' displayed here comprises of 'Usr' + 'Sys' + 'Guest' components.

Note: At the moment, the 'IO Wait' component is not part of the 'CPU Time' shown under this graph. For 'IO Wait' statistics, please refer to the 'CPU' graph under the 'server' page of the respective hosts.

</DDP_Bubble_415_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_CPU_Usage> <DDP_Bubble_416_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_CPU_Steal>

The graph displays the sum of the maximum CPU steal (in minutes) of all the VMs (on y-axis) for every 15 Min interval (on x-axis) for the last 10 days.

The 'CPU Steal (in minutes)' is derived from the 'Steal (%)' stats of 'sar' data as 'cpu_steal_min = ((steal_percentage/100) x number_of_processors)' .

</DDP_Bubble_416_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_CPU_Steal> <DDP_Bubble_417_Res_Usg_Last_N_Days_VM_Memory_Usage>

These 'Memory Usage (in MB)' stats are obtained from 'sar' data and comprises of 'Used' + 'Buffers' + 'Cached' components.

The "PM 15MIN ROP Duration" graph is generated from the data collected from 'PMIC_FILE_COLLECTION_STATISTICS' log lines logged to Elasticsearch. The graph displays the file-collection duration (difference between 'fileCollectionStartTime' and 'ropEndTime' ) per each 15MIN ROP for the last 31 days.

Where  fileCollectionStartTime'  = ropIdentifier + collection delay offset + ROP interval

The below data is obtained from ROS-PTAF.log file(<bur>) based on KEYWORD|Starting|Finished loglines logged to ROS-PTAF.log.* files.

'NA' value indicates End of the operation is not received in log file.

</DDP_Bubble_425_ENM_Bur_Restore_Logs> <DDP_Bubble_426_BUR_Restore_Throughput_Daily_Totals>

The Restore (BUR) throughput details are retrieved from 'measurement_restore_FilesystemThroughput.data' logs. The 'Daily Totals' table displays the following information:

  • Start Time: The start time of the earliest filesytem-restore among all the hosts for the given restore.
  • End Time: The end time of the filesystem back that finished last among all the hosts for the given restore.
  • Restore: The keyword of the given restore.
  • Overall Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under all the hosts with the total time (in sec) taken for all those filesystem-restores under all those hosts.
  • Overall Parallel Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under all the hosts with the time difference between the start time of the earliest filesystem-restore (among all the hosts) and the end time of the latest filesystem-restore (among all the hosts). Note: The 'Overall Parallel Throughput' generally tends to be larger than 'Overall Throughput' since the time used to calculate the former spans multiple filesystem-restores running in parallel.
  • Num of Filesystems: The total number of filesystems that have been backed-up across all the hosts.
  • Total Size (MB): The total size of the data that has been backed-up across all the filesystems and hosts.

Note: SFS restore data is not collected at this time so throughput data rates have to be considered in that light.

</DDP_Bubble_426_BUR_Restore_Throughput_Daily_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_427_BUR_Restore_Throughput_Details>

The Restore (BUR) throughput details are retrieved from 'measurement_restore_FilesystemThroughput.data' logs. The 'Throughput Details' table displays the following information:

  • Start Time: The start time of the restore operation for the given filesystem under the given host.
  • End Time: The end time of the restore operation for the given filesystem under the given host.
  • Restore: The keyword of the given restore.
  • Host: The hostname of the server whose filesystem is getting backed-up.
  • Throughput (MB/sec): The throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for the given filesystem under the given host with the total time (in sec) taken for that restore operation (i.e., difference between the start and end times).
  • Backup Mount Point: The path to backup mount point.
  • Filesystem: The filesystem that is getting backed-up.
  • Filesystem Used Size (MB): The size of data available under the filesystem at the time of restore.
  • Filesystem Total Size (MB): The total size of the filesystem

</DDP_Bubble_427_BUR_Restore_Throughput_Details> <DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Queues>

  • Message Count: Number of messages currently held in this queue awaiting delivery.

Note: Information about each queue and topic is  here .

The SFS Backup throughput details are retrieved from 'measurement_backup_FilesystemThroughput.data' logs. The 'Daily Totals' table displays the following information:

    Start Time: The start time of the earliest filesytem-backup for the given backup

    End Time: The end time of the filesystem back that finished last backup

    Backup: The keyword of the given backup.

    Overall Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under SFS host with the total time (in sec) taken for all those filesystem-backups under all those hosts.

    Overall Parallel Throughput (MB/sec): The overall throughput calculated by dividing the total size (in MB) of data backed-up for all the filesystems under SFS with the time difference between the start time of the earliest filesystem-backup and the end time of the latest filesystem-backup. Note: The 'Overall Parallel Throughput' generally tends to be larger than 'Overall Throughput' since the time used to calculate the former spans multiple filesystem-backups running in parallel.

    Num of Filesystems: The total number of filesystems that have been backed-up under SFS.

    Total Size (MB): The total size of the data that has been backed-up across all the filesystems and SFS host.

</DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Top_Notification_Nodes> <DDP_Bubble.notif_analysis.nodeEvictionDetails>

This information is taken from CPP CM Notification (MSCM) logs from ElasticSearch.

Time : the time of the buffer notification completed.

MSCM Instance : the instance name of the server.

Network Element : Name of the Network Element.

Evicted Notifications : Count of the Evicted Notifications.

Large & Small node caches are separate buffers which hold notifications for the Large (>=15000 Mos size) & Small (<15000 Mos size) nodes respectively.

Notifications are buffered in the following cases:
1. When node sync is in progress
2. When expected notification (based on GC) does not arrive and next notification arrives instead. So this current notification has to buffered for future processing.

</DDP_Bubble.notif_analysis.nodeEvictionDetails> <DDP_Bubble.molist.enmMoRatioforERBS_NODE_MODEL>

The below table displays the Mo Ratio Analysis for models like ERBS,RNC,Lrat for a specified set of Mos per model as listed in the story: TORF-240004.

The ratio in the last column is computed as the quotient of "Live Mo Count for that specific Model and Mo combination" and the "Live Mo Count of reference cells of that model".

Reference Cells are: UtranCell in case of RNC Model, EUtranCellTDD and EUtranCellFDD in case of ERBS and Lrat Models.

Note: If at any case, the Live Cell Count for the reference cells per model are Null, then the Mo Ratio is being set to "".

</DDP_Bubble.molist.enmMoRatioforERBS_NODE_MODEL> <DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Full_Sync_Totals>

This data is retrieved from the Elasticsearch.

  • MSCMIP Instance : The instance number of the MSCMIP cluster
  • #Syncs : The total number of Syncs on the specified Instance or the total number across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Avg Duration : The average duration time [hh:mm:ss] of syncs on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Avg MOs/Sec : The average number of Managed Objects per second synced on the specified Instance or the average across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Max Duration : The maximium duration [hh:mm:ss] of a sync on the specified Instance or the maximum duration across all Instances where Instance equals Totals
  • Total MOs Parsed : The total number of Managed Objects parsed on the specified Instance or the total parsed across all Instances where Instance equals Totals

</DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Full_Sync_Totals> <DDP_Bubble.ip_transport_stats.Full_Sync_Stats>

This data is taken from the Elasticsearch/Logstash log server where each stage of a successful sync is logged.

  • Start Time: The time [hh:mm:ss] that the sync started.
  • Network Element: Network Element.
  • MSCMIP Instance: Instance of MSCMIP.
  • NE Type: Type of Network Element
  • Sync Type: Type of sync performed
  • Num Total MOs Parsed: Total number of Managed Objects 
  • Total Time(ms): Total Duration(in ms) of Bulk Sync.
  • MOs Parsed/sec: Number of Managed Objects parsed.
  • Num ECIM MOs Parsed: Number of ECIM Managed Objects Parsed.
  • Time Read ECIM MOs from NE(ms): Time taken(in ms) in reading response from Node.
  • Time Transformed ECIM MOs from NE(ms): Time taken(in ms) in transforming node response to ENM Database objects
  • Num YANG MOs Parsed: Number of YANG Managed Objects parsed. 
  • Time Read YANG MOs from NE(ms): Time taken(in ms) in YANG MOs from Node. 
  • Time Read MOs from NE(ms): Time taken(in ms) in persisting Managed Objects.
  • Time Transformed YANG MOs from NE(ms): Time taken(in ms) in tranforming YANG MOs from Network Element
  • Time Total Transformed MOs from NE(ms):Total time taken(in ms) in tranforming MOs from Network Element
  • Num MOs Write:Time taken(in ms) in persisting Managed Objects
  • Time MOs Write(ms):Time taken(in ms) in persisting Managed Objects
  • Time MOs Delta Calculation(ms):Time taken(in ms) in Calculating Delta between ENM database ManagedObjects and Node Response. This field is not valid for first Sync.
  • Num ECIM MOs Attribute Read: Number of ECIM Managed Objects attributes read from Node.
  • Num ECIM MOs Attribute Transformed: Number of ECIM Managed Objects attributes transformed to ENM Database Objects attributes.
  • Num ECIM MOs Attribute Null: Number of ECIM ENM Managed Objects attributes found null on node.
  • Num ECIM MOs Attribute Error in Transformation: Number of error encountered during ECIM Managed Objects attributes transformation.
  • Num ECIM MOs Mo Error: Number of error encountered during ECIM Managed Objects.

</DDP_Bubble_464_ENM_SOCKETS_STATES> <DDP_Bubble_465_PMIC_ROP_Pull_Totals>

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PULL") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:35 and hh:50 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

</DDP_Bubble_465_PMIC_ROP_Pull_Totals> <DDP_Bubble_466_PMIC_ROP_Push_Totals>

If the PM FLS is available an additional table (called "PULL") will be shown which shows a breakdown of file type collected per node type. This information is obtained from the FLS Database via PSQL (e.g. file creation  time in OSS, ROP start time, ROP end time). Additional information can be plotted from this table which shows:

  • Files: Number of files collected in the File Collection cycles (FCC). It includes all files collected in this FCC so could also include files collected for other ROPs. The FCC for 15 min ROPs typically start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50.
  • Volume: Volume.
  • Duration: How long the FCC took. It considers each FCC to last 15 mins and start at hh:05, hh:20, hh:35 or hh:50 and looks for the time the last file was collected in that FCC.
  • Files outside FCC: Files collected in this FCC which should have been collected in a previous FCC. e.g. A file for a ROP from hh:15 to hh:30 should be in the FCC between hh:35 and hh:50 otherwise it is counted as a file that is outside this FCC.

</DDP_Bubble.cm_templates.timing> <DDP_Bubble.modelling.mdt>

This data is collected from elasticsearch logs

  • Start Time: The time of day the MDT execution started.
  • Total Time: The total duration of MDT execution.
  • Phase 1 Time: The duration of MDT phase 1.
  • Phase 2 Time: The duration of MDT phase 2.
  • Phase 3 Time: The duration of MDT phase 3.
  • Model Root Dir I/O: The time taken to write all models to the file system.
  • Deployed Models: The total number of models passed into MDT, including duplicates.
  • Un-deployed Models: The number of un-deployed models.
  • Unique Models: The number of models deployed with unique model URNs.
  • New Models: The number of unique newly-deployed models, i.e. models for which no other model with the same URN was already deployed.
  • Overwritten Models: The number of unique overwritten models, i.e. models for which a model with the same URN was already deployed, but without a matching hash.
  • Not-written Models: The number of unique models deployed but not written to the file system because a model with a matching hash was already written.
  • Models Validated: The number of models validated during MDT execution.
  • Dependencies Calculated: The number of models for which dependencies were calculated during MDT execution.
  • Model JARs: The number of model JARs passed into MDT.
  • JARs with Model Meta Info: The number of model JARs containing a modelMetaInfo.xml file.

</DDP_Bubble.modelling.mdt> <DDP_Bubble.modelling.tmi>

Removed TMIs

  • NE Type: the Network Element type (i.e. ERBS, RadioNode, etc).
  • Target Model Identity (TMI): this is a string representing the TMI that has been removed from ENM.

Added TMIs

  • NE Type: the Network Element type (i.e. ERBS, RadioNode etc).
  • Target Model Identity (TMI): this is a string representing the TMI that has been introduced in ENM.

</DDP_Bubble.node_security_workflows.Workflow_Help> <DDP_Bubble.ap_daily_metrics.ApZeroTouchStats>

Data  is collected from the  'INTEGRATION_BIND' & 'MIGRATION_BIND'  log lines under the Elasticsearch logs.

Project Name: The name of the project which contains the node that bind was executed against.

Node Name: The name of the node that bind was executed against.

Node Type: The type of node that the bind was executed against.

Bind Type: The type of bind that was executed, late bind is for when the user executes the binding after ordering the node, early binding is where the user executes the binding as part of the ordering of the node.

Activity Type: The Activity Type that was executed.

</DDP_Bubble.ecim_med.COMECIM_RATE> <DDP_Bubble.modelling.cacheUsage>

Below graphs represent data of Model Cache Usage collected from MBean  com.ericsson.oss.itpf.modeling.modelservice:type=ModelServiceCache

  • CACHE SIZE: The number of entries in the cache. A model may have more than one entry in the cache, with the different entries being applicable to different target types.
  • CACHE MISSES: The number of requests that required external retrieval of a model as opposed to read directly from the cache.
  • CACHE REQUESTS: The total number of requests that are made to retrieve a model.
  • MODEL COUNT: The number of models in the cache.
  • CACHE HIT %: (numberOfCacheRequests -numberOfCacheMisses)/numberOfCacheRequests * 100)
  • CACHE DESCRIPTION TEXTS:   Property describing if description texts within models are to be replaced with empty strings or not. The default is {@code ALL} (indicated by the value zero) meaning that by default all description texts are cached. {@code NONE} (indicated by the value of one) is the only other valid value; in this case model description texts will be replaced by empty strings.
  • MAX CACHE IDLE TIME (sec): The amount of time (in seconds) an entry in the cache can be idle before eviction. The default is -1 and is interpreted as unlimited lifespan within the cache.
  • MAX CACHE SIZE:  The maximum number of entries allowed in the model service cache. A value of zero indicates that cache eviction is not enabled and therefore an unlimited amount of entries is allowed
  • CACHE EVICTIONS:  The number of models evicted from the cache.
  • READWRITE RATIO:  The read/write ratio of the cache. The value displayed is rounded to the nearest whole number

ddp_instr_model=[TOR/common/enm_shmmodeling_instr]

</DDP_Bubble.modelling.cacheUsage>
